Hunting with Trained Animals: Conditions and Proof
Ruling with proof on hunting with trained animals and its conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for lawful hunting with trained animals and apply the hadith of 'Adi ibn Hatim to determine the ruling in various scenarios.

Core Idea
A trained animal that eats its prey makes it haram — the catch is for itself, not for you.

Hunting is a permissible means of obtaining food, but it comes with specific conditions derived from the Quran and Sunnah. In this lesson, we examine the ruling on hunting with trained predatory animals, the proof from Surah al-Ma'idah and the hadith of 'Adi ibn Hatim, and the detailed conditions that determine whether the game is halal or haram.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Hunting with trained animals is mubah (permissible) under specific conditions. The author states this clearly.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is Quran 5:4 and the hadith of 'Adi ibn Hatim from Bukhari and Muslim. Both are quoted in the passage.
The Quranic verse provides the general permission; the hadith details the conditions.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'fakulu' in the verse indicates permission (ibaha). The hadith restricts this permission: if the animal eats, it is not halal; if another untrained animal joins, it is not halal.
The phrase 'imasaak 'ala nafsihi' shows the dog caught for itself.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some schools require the trainer to be Muslim; Hanafis allow a Kitabi (People of the Book). The passage does not address this, but it is a known difference.
This lesson focuses on the conditions stated in the texts.
5
Evaluate the conditions
From the hadith, three key conditions emerge: (1) tasmiyah when releasing, (2) the dog must not eat from the prey, (3) no other untrained dog joins without tasmiyah.
These are found in the explicit words of the Prophet.

كتاب الصيد والذبائح 
ضروری نوٹ : صید کا معنی شکار کرنا ہے۔ اگر کتا یا بازسکھایا ہوا ہو اور بسم اللہ پڑھ کر چھوڑ دے اور شکار ذبح کرنے پر قدرت سے پہلے مر جائے تب بھی حلال ہے۔ یا بسم اللہ کر کے تیر پھینکے اور مر جائے تب بھی حلال ہے۔ دلیل اس آیت میں ہے۔ یسئلونك ماذا احل لهم قل احل لكم الطيبات وما علمتم من الجوارح مكلبين تعلمونهن مما علمكم الله فكلوا مما امسكن عليكم و اذكروا اسم الله علیه (الف) ( آیت سورۃ المائدۃ ۵) اس آیت میں جتلایا کہ کتے کو سکھاؤ پھر سکھایا ہوا کتے کو بسم اللہ پڑھ کر شکار پر چھوڑ دو تو وہ جو کچھ تمہارے لئے رو کے یعنی مار لائے لیکن اس میں سے خود نہ کھائے تو وہ شکار تمہارے لئے حلال ہے (۲) اور حدیث میں ہے۔ سمعت عدی بن حاتم قال سألت رسول الله الا اللهم عن المعراض فقال اذا اصبت بحده فكل فاذا اصاب بعرضه فقتل فانه وقيذ فيه تأكل فقلت ارسل کلبی ؟ قال اذا ارسلت کلبک و سمیت فكل قلت فان اكل ؟قال فلا تأكل فانه لم يمسک علیک انما امسک علی نفسه. قلت ارسل کلبی فاجد معه كلبا آخر؟ قال لاتأكل فانک انما سمیت علی کلبک ولم تسم على الآخر (ب) ( بخاری شریف ، باب صید المعراض ص ۸۲۳ نمبر ۵۴۷۶، کتاب الذبائح والصيد ومسلم شریف، باب الصيد بالكلاب المعلمة والرمی ص ۱۳۵ نمبر ۴۹۷۴/۱۹۲۹) اس حدیث سے شکار کے تمام بنیادی مسائل معلوم ہوتے 
ہیں۔ 
[۲۵۸۰] (۱) جائز ہے شکار کرنا سکھائے ہوئے کتے ، چیتے ، باز اور تمام سکھائے ہوئے پھاڑ کھانے والے جانور سے۔ کتا ہو، چیتا ہو، باز ہو یا دوسرے زخمی کرنے والے جانور ہوں ان کو ان کے طریقے پر شکار کرنا سکھایا ہو اور آپ کا فرماں بردار ہوان 
سے شکار کرنا جائز ہے۔ او پر آیت میں وما علمتم من الجوارح مكلبين تعلمونهن ( آیت ۴ سورۃ المائدة (۵) اس آیت سے معلوم ہوا کہ پھاڑ کھانے والے جانور کو شکار کرنا سکھایا ہو تو اس سے شکار کرنا جائز ہے۔ اس میں کتا، چیتا، باز جن جانور کے گوشت نہ کھائے جاتے ہوں وہ سب آگئے حاشیہ : (الف) لوگ پوچھتے ہیں کہ ان کے لئے کیا حلال ہے؟ آپ کہہ دیجئے آپ کے لئے حلال ہے پاک چیزیں اور جو تم نے سکھلایا پھاڑنے والے جانور کو، اس کو سکھلاؤ جو اللہ نے تم کو سکھلایا۔ پس کھاؤ جو تمہارے لئے روکا اور جانور پر اللہ کا نام پڑھو۔ یعنی جانوروں کو شکار کرناسکھاؤ، پس وہ شکار کر کے تمہارے لئے چھوڑ دیں اور شکاری جانور کو بسم اللہ کہ کر چھوڑے ہو تو اس شکار کو کھا ؤ (ب) میں نے حضور سے تیر کے بارے میں پوچھا تو فرمایا اگر دھار کی جانب سے لگا ہو تو شکار کھاؤ اور اگر بے دھار کی جانب سے لگا ہوا اور مرگیا ہو تو وہ وقیذ یعنی چور کر کے مارا ہوا ہے۔ اس لئے مت کھاؤ۔ میں نے پوچھا اپنا کتا شکار پر بھیجتا ہوں فرمایا اگر اپنے کتے کو بھیجا اور بسم اللہ پڑھا تو کھاؤ۔ میں نے پوچھا اگر کتا کھالے تو ؟ فرمایا مت کھاؤ اس لئے کہ تمہارے لئے شکار نہیں کیا ہے اس نے اپنے لئے شکار کیا ہے۔ میں نے پوچھا اپنا کتا چھوڑتا ہوں تو دوسرے کتے بھی شامل ہو جاتے ہیں تو کیا کروں؟ فرمایا مت کھاؤ کیونکہ اپنے کتے پر ہم اللہ پڑھے ہو دوسرے کے کتے پر بسم اللہ نہیں 
پڑھے ہو۔
Book of Hunting
Book of Hunting and Slaughtering
[2580] (1) It is permissible to hunt with the trained dog, cheetah, falcon, and all trained predatory animals.
Book of Hunting and Slaughtering
Necessary Note: The meaning of sayd is hunting. If a dog or falcon is trained, and one releases it while reciting Bismillah, and the game dies before one is able to slaughter it, it is still halal. Or if one throws an arrow while reciting Bismillah and it dies, it is also halal. The proof is in this verse: "They ask you what is permitted to them. Say: Permitted to you are good things and what you have taught of predatory animals, training them as dogs. You teach them of what Allah has taught you. So eat of what they hold for you and mention the name of Allah over it." (Surah al-Ma'idah 5) This verse teaches that you train dogs, then release a trained dog while reciting Bismillah over the game, and what it catches and holds for you without eating from it, that game is halal for you. (2) And in the hadith: I heard 'Adi ibn Hatim say: I asked the Messenger of Allah (may Allah bless him and grant him peace) about the mi'rad (a blunt arrow). He said: "If you hit with its sharp edge, eat; but if you hit with its blunt side and it kills, then it is waqidh (a blow) – do not eat." I said: "I send my dog?" He said: "If you send your dog and mention the name of Allah, then eat." I said: "If it eats?" He said: "Then do not eat, for it did not hold for you; it held for itself." I said: "I send my dog and find another dog with it?" He said: "Do not eat, for you mentioned the name of Allah on your dog and not on the other." (Bukhari, Bab Sayd al-Mi'rad, p. 823 no. 5476, Kitab al-Dhaba'ih wa al-Sayd; Muslim, Bab al-Sayd bi al-Kilab al-Mu'allamah wa al-Ramy, p. 135 no. 4974/1929) From this hadith, all basic issues of hunting are known.
[2580] (1) It is permissible to hunt with the trained dog, cheetah, falcon, and all trained carnivorous animals. Whether dog, cheetah, falcon, or other wounding animals, if they have been taught to hunt in their manner and are obedient, hunting with them is permissible. From the above verse: "And what you have taught of predatory animals, training them as dogs" (Surah al-Ma'idah 5:4), it is understood that if a predatory animal has been taught to hunt, then hunting with it is permissible. This includes dogs, cheetahs, falcons, and any animal whose meat is not eaten. 
Marginal note: (a) People ask what is permissible for them. Say: Permissible for you are good things and what you have taught of predatory animals, teaching them from what Allah has taught you. So eat of what they hold for you and mention the name of Allah over the animal. That is, teach animals to hunt, then they hunt and leave it for you, and if you have released the hunting animal with Bismillah, then eat that game. 
(b) I asked the Prophet about the arrow: He said if it hits with the sharp edge, eat the game; if it hits with the blunt side and dies, then it is waqidh, i.e., killed by a blow, so do not eat. I asked: I send my dog? He said: If you send your dog and recite Bismillah, then eat. I asked: If the dog eats? He said: Do not eat, because it did not hunt for you, it hunted for itself. I asked: I send my dog and another dog joins? He said: Do not eat, because you recited Bismillah on your dog, not on the other dog.
Source pages p. 11

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Book of Hunting (Kitab al-Sayd). The author states the basic ruling: it is permissible to hunt with trained predatory animals such as dogs, cheetahs, and falcons. The term 'mu'allam' (trained) is key – the animal must be trained to hunt and obey commands. The proof is presented from Quran 5:4, which explicitly permits eating what trained predators catch for you, provided you mention Allah's name when releasing them. The author then explains the hadith of 'Adi ibn Hatim, which elaborates conditions: if the trained animal eats from the prey, it is not halal because it caught it for itself; if another untrained animal joins, the prey is not halal due to lack of tasmiyah on that animal. The author also discusses the mi'rad (a blunt arrow), distinguishing between a clean hit with the sharp edge (permissible) and a blunt impact (not permissible, as it is like a blow). The overall message is that hunting is halal with proper conditions, and the sources clarify the details.

Key Terms
الكلب المعلم (al-kalb al-mu'allam): A dog that has been trained to hunt, respond to commands, and refrain from eating the prey.
الجوارح (al-jawarih): Predatory animals that hunt by using their claws or fangs, such as dogs, cheetahs, falcons, etc.
المعراض (al-mi'rad): A type of arrow that is blunt and does not have a sharp edge; it kills by striking rather than piercing.
الوقيذ (al-waqidh): An animal killed by a blow or blunt force without a sharp cut; considered carrion and not halal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith of 'Adi ibn Hatim, if a trained dog eats from the prey after catching it, what is the ruling?
A) The remaining meat is halal
B) The prey is haram because the dog caught it for itself
C) It is halal if the hunter recites tasmiyah again
D) It is halal because the dog is trained

Key Takeaway
Hunting with trained animals is halal only if the animal is trained, tasmiyah is recited, and the animal does not eat from the prey or participate with another untrained animal.

Permissibility of Hunting with Trained Predatory Animals
Ruling on hunting with trained animals and its proof from Quran and Sunnah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for halal hunting with trained animals and apply the Hanafi ruling to scenarios involving trained dogs and falcons.

Core Idea
A trained animal's catch is halal only if Bismillah is recited and the animal does not eat from it.

Hunting is a means of obtaining food that predates Islam. The Shariah sets clear conditions to ensure the meat is lawful. This lesson examines the Qur'anic permission and the Prophetic details that define when game caught by trained animals is halal. You will learn the essential conditions and a key difference with the Shafi'i school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
State the basic ruling: hunting with trained animals (dogs, falcons, etc.) is permissible (mubah).
The passage begins: 'It is permissible to hunt with the trained dog...'
2
List the conditions for halal consumption
Extract the conditions from the commentary and hadith: the animal must be trained, Bismillah must be recited at release, the trained animal must not eat from the catch, and if using an arrow it must hit with the sharp edge.
The hadith adds the condition about the dog not eating and about a second dog.
3
Analyze the Qur'anic proof
Read the verse (Surah al-Ma'idah 5:4) and explain how it proves permissibility and the condition that the animal catches 'for you'.
The imperative 'kulu' (eat) indicates permission; 'what they catch for you' implies for the hunter, not for the animal.
4
Examine the hadith of Adi ibn Hatim
Work through the hadith: what it rules about the mi'rad, the dog releasing, and the dog eating.
The hadith is the primary source for the condition that if the dog eats, the catch is haram.
5
Apply to a scenario
Given a scenario: a trained dog catches a rabbit, eats part of it, but the hunter recites Bismillah. Determine the ruling and state why.
Use the hadith: 'If it eats, do not eat, for it caught for itself.'

الشرح الثميرى الجزء الرابع )
كتاب الصيد
كتاب الصيد والذبائح
[۲۵۸۰]( ۱ ) يجوز الاصطياد بالكلب المعلم والفهد والبازى وسائر الجوارح المعلمة .
كتاب الصيد والذبائح
ضروری نوٹ : صید کا معنی شکار کرنا ہے۔ اگر کتا یا بازسکھایا ہوا ہو اور بسم اللہ پڑھ کر چھوڑ دے اور شکار ذبح کرنے پر قدرت سے پہلے مر جائے تب بھی حلال ہے۔ یا بسم اللہ کر کے تیر پھینکے اور مر جائے تب بھی حلال ہے۔ دلیل اس آیت میں ہے۔ یسئلونک ماذا احل لهم قل احل لكم الطيبات وما علمتم من الجوارح مكلبين تعلمونهن مما علمكم الله فكلوا مما امسكن عليكم و اذكروا اسم الله علیه (الف) ( آیت سورۃ المائدۃ ۵) اس آیت میں جتلایا کہ کتے کو سکھاؤ پھر سکھایا ہوا کتے کو بسم اللہ پڑھ کر شکار پر چھوڑ دو تو وہ جو کچھ تمہارے لئے رو کے یعنی مار لائے لیکن اس میں سے خود نہ کھائے تو وہ شکار تمہارے لئے حلال ہے (۲) اور حدیث میں ہے۔ سمعت عدی بن حاتم قال سألت رسول الله الا اللهم عن المعراض فقال اذا اصبت بحده فكل فاذا اصاب بعرضه فقتل فانه وقيذ فيه تأكل فقلت ارسل کلبی ؟ قال اذا ارسلت کلبک و سمیت فكل قلت فان اكل ؟قال فلا تأكل فانه لم يمسک علیک انما امسک علی نفسه. قلت ارسل کلبی فاجد معه كلبا آخر؟ قال لاتأکل فانک انما سمیت علی کلبک ولم تسم على الآخر (ب) ( بخاری شریف ، باب صید المعراض ص ۸۲۳ نمبر ۵۴۷۶، کتاب الذبائح والصيد ومسلم شریف، باب الصيد بالكلاب المعلمة والرمی ص ۱۳۵ نمبر ۴۹۷۴/۱۹۲۹) اس حدیث سے شکار کے تمام بنیادی مسائل معلوم ہوتے ہیں۔
Al-Sharh al-Thamiri vol. 4. Book of Hunting. Book of Hunting and Slaughtered Animals. [2580] (1) It is permissible to hunt with the trained dog, cheetah, falcon, and all trained predators. Note: The meaning of sayd is hunting. If a dog or falcon is trained and you release it with Bismillah, and the game dies before you are able to slaughter it, it is halal. Or if you shoot an arrow with Bismillah and it dies, it is halal. The proof is in this verse: 'They ask you what has been made lawful for them. Say: Lawful for you are good things and that which you have taught the hunting animals, training them as you have been taught by Allah. So eat of what they catch for you and mention the name of Allah upon it.' (Surah al-Ma'idah 5:4) This verse indicates: teach the dog, then release the trained dog with Bismillah on the hunt; whatever it catches for you, i.e., kills, but does not eat from it, then that game is halal for you. (2) And in the hadith: I heard Adi ibn Hatim said: I asked the Messenger of Allah about the mi'rad (a pointed arrow). He said: 'If you hit with its sharp edge, eat; if you hit with its blunt side and it kills, then it is a wathil; do not eat.' I said: I release my dog? He said: 'If you release your dog and mention the name of Allah, eat.' I said: If it eats? He said: 'Do not eat, for it did not catch for you; it caught for itself.' I said: I release my dog and find another dog with it? He said: 'Do not eat, for you mentioned Allah's name on your dog but not on the other.' (Bukhari, Bab Sayd al-Mi'rad, p.823 no.5476, Kitab al-Dhaba'ih wa al-Sayd; Muslim, Bab al-Sayd bi al-Kilab al-Mu'allamah wa al-Rami, p.135 no.4974/1929) From this hadith, all basic rulings of hunting are known.
Source pages p. 11

Commentary
This passage begins with a ruling statement from the matn: It is permissible to hunt with trained predatory animals such as dogs, cheetahs, and falcons, as well as all other trained predators. The word 'jawaarih' refers to beasts of prey that wound. The commentary then provides a necessary note explaining the meaning of sayd (hunting) and conditions: if a trained dog or falcon is released with the recitation of Bismillah, and the game dies before the hunter reaches it, it is halal. Similarly, if an arrow is shot with Bismillah and the game dies, it is halal. The primary proof is the Qur'anic verse (Surah al-Ma'idah 5:4), which is quoted in full: 'They ask you what has been made lawful for them...' The verse explicitly permits the catch of trained hunting animals when Bismillah is said, provided the animal does not eat from the catch. The author then explains the verse: one must train the dog, then release it with Bismillah; if it catches and kills but does not eat, the game is halal. The second proof is the well-known hadith of Adi ibn Hatim, transmitted in Bukhari and Muslim. The hadith covers several key rulings: (1) hitting game with the sharp edge of an arrow (mi'rad) makes it halal, but hitting with the blunt side results in a wathil (killed by blunt force) which is not halal. (2) Releasing a trained dog with Bismillah makes the catch halal. (3) If the dog eats from the catch, it is not halal because it caught for itself. (4) If another untrained dog joins and partakes, the catch is not halal because Bismillah was not recited for the other dog. This hadith forms the foundation of the rulings on hunting with dogs and arrows. The passage ends by noting that from this hadith all basic principles of hunting are derived. The Hanafi school follows these texts, emphasizing the conditions of training, reciting Bismillah, and ensuring the animal does not consume the catch.

Key Terms
الاصطياد (al-iṣṭiyād): Hunting, the act of pursuing and capturing game animals.
المعلم (al-muʿallam): Trained (animal), one that has been taught to hunt and obey commands.
الجوارح (al-jawāriḥ): Predators that hunt and wound; beasts of prey that kill by tearing.
المعراض (al-miʿrāḍ): A pointed arrow used for hunting, which can hit with its sharp edge or blunt side.
الوَقِيذ (al-waqīdh): An animal killed by blunt force (e.g., hit with the side of an arrow), which is not halal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith of Adi ibn Hatim, if a hunter releases his trained dog with Bismillah and the dog catches a rabbit and eats part of it, what is the ruling on that rabbit?
A) It is halal because the dog was trained and Bismillah was recited.
B) It is halal only if the rabbit was still alive when reached.
C) It is haram because the dog ate from it, indicating it caught for itself.
D) It is makruh but permissible.

Key Takeaway
Hunting with trained animals is permissible, but the game is only halal if Bismillah is recited, the animal does not eat from the catch, and no untrained animal joins without a separate tasmiya.

Defining Trained Hunting Animals and Their Use in Hunting
Defines training and details three hunting methods with conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi criteria for training a dog and a falcon, list the three methods of hunting, and identify the conditions that validate each method.

Core Idea
A trained dog leaves food; a trained falcon returns when called.

The Hanafi school distinguishes between dogs and birds of prey based on their nature: dogs are domestic animals that instinctively eat the catch, so training means overcoming that instinct; birds are wild, so training means becoming responsive. The same distinction applies to the permissibility of the catch if the animal eats part of it. This lesson unpacks the definitions and the three recognized hunting methods with their conditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition of a trained dog
Find the passage that states a dog is considered trained if it leaves the game uneaten three times. Note that this is a behavioral test, not just physical ability.
The dog must not eat skin, flesh, or bones.
2
Identify the definition of a trained falcon
Find the passage that states a falcon is trained if it returns when called after being released for the hunt. This is tested three times.
Birds are wild; training is shown by obedience, not by leaving food.
3
List the three methods of hunting
The passage mentions three methods: with predatory animals (dogs, cheetahs), with birds of prey (falcons, shikra), and with projectiles (arrows, guns). For each, note the conditions required for the catch to be halal.
All three methods require Bismillah at release.
4
Determine when the catch is halal
For each method, check the conditions: for predators, the animal must not eat; for birds, eating does not render haram if Bismillah was said; for projectiles, the sharp part must wound. Also note the opportunity to slaughter: if alive and reachable, the hunter must slaughter; otherwise the catch is halal if it dies from the wound.
If the hunter reaches the game alive and can slaughter but does not, the catch becomes haram.

الشرح الثميرى الجزء الرابع
كتاب الصيد
[۲۵] (۲) وتعليم الكلب ان يترك الاكل ثلث مرات وتعليم البازي ان يرجع اذا ان سكھوں سے شکار کرنا جائز ہے۔
شکار کی تفصیل یہ ہے کہ تین طریقوں سے شکار کرتے ہیں (۱) پھاڑ کھانے والے جانوروں کے ذریعہ جیسے کتا، چیتا۔ ان سے شکار کی تین شرطیں ہیں۔ پہلی کتا سکھایا ہوا ہو، کتے کو سکھانے کا طریقہ یہ ہے کہ تین بار شکار پکڑے اور اس کی کھال، گوشت اور ہڈی وغیرہ کتانہ کھائے بلکہ مالک کے لئے چھوڑ دے تو شریعت کی نگاہ میں کتا سکھایا ہوا سمجھا جائے گا۔ تمام پھاڑ کھانے والے جانور کے سکھانے کا طریقہ یہی ہے۔ اور دوسری شرط یہ ہے کہ بسم اللہ پڑھ کر جانور کو چھوڑا ہو۔ اور تیسری شرط یہ ہے کہ پھاڑ کھانے والا جانور شکار کرنے کے بعد اس میں سے کھائے نہیں۔ ایسی صورت میں جانور نے شکار کیا اور شکار ذبح کرنے سے پہلے مرگیا تو وہ شکار حلال ہے۔ اور شکار زندہ تھا اس حال میں شکار کو مالک نے پکڑا ذبح کرنے کا موقع تھا اور ذبح نہیں کیا تو اب حلال نہیں ہوگا۔ اور ذبح کرنے کا موقع نہیں تھا اور شکار مر گیا تو حلال ہوگا۔ پس اگر شکار کرنے والے جانور نے شکار کرنے کے بعد شکار کو کھا لیا تو مالک کے لئے یہ شکار حلال نہیں رہا۔ اور ایک روایت میں یہ ہے کہ شکار کے بدن میں کہیں زخمی بھی کیا ہو جو ذبح اضطراری کے درجے میں ہو گیا اور گلا گھونٹنے کے درجے میں نہ رہا۔
شکار کرنے کا دوسرا طریقہ یہ ہے کہ پرندہ مثلا باز، شکرہ وغیرہ سے شکار کرے۔ اس میں تین شرطیں ہیں۔ ایک تو یہ کہ پرندہ سکھایا ہوا ہو۔ اس کو سکھانے کا طریقہ یہ ہے کہ اس کو چھوڑ نے تو شکار کے لئے جائے اور روکے تو رک جائے ۔ تین بار ایسے کرنے سے شریعت کی نگاہ میں یہ پرندہ سکھایا ہوا ہے۔ کتے کی طرح کھانے اور نہ کھانے کے اعتبار سے اس کے سکھانے کا مدار نہیں ہے۔ اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ پرندہ متوحش جانور ہے اس لئے وہ بلانے سے بار بار آجائے اور اپنی فطری عادت تو حش کو چھوڑ دے یہی اس کے سکھانے کی علامت ہے۔ اور کتا پالتو جانور ہے وہ آدمی کے پاس گھوم گھوم کر آتا ہے۔ البتہ وہ شکار کو پکڑنے کے بعد کھانے کی کوشش کرتا ہے اس لئے وہ فطری عادت چھوڑ دے اور مالک کے لئے تین بار نہ کھائے تو یہ اس کے معلم ہونے یعنی سیکھے ہوئے ہونے کی علامت ہے۔ اور دوسری شرط یہ ہے کہ بسم اللہ پڑھ کر شکار پر چھوڑے۔ اب اگر وہ شکار میں سے کھا بھی لے تب بھی مالک کے لئے حلال ہے۔ البتہ شکار ہاتھ میں آنے کے بعد اتنا موقع ہو کہ ذبح کر سکے اور نہیں کیا تو مالک کے لئے حلال نہیں ہے۔ اور اگر اتنا موقع نہیں تھا کہ ذبح کرے اور مرگیا تب بھی شکار حلال ہے۔ اور ایک روایت کے مطابق تیسری شرط یہ ہے کہ کہیں زخمی بھی کیا ہو کیونکہ آیت میں وما علمتم من الجوارح ہے۔ اور جوارح کا ترجمہ ہے کہ زخمی کرنے والا ہو۔ اور شکار کرنے کا تیسرا طریقہ یہ ہے کہ تیر یا بندوق کے ذریعہ شکار کرے۔ اس سے شکار کرنے کی تین شرطیں ہیں۔ ایک تو یہ ہے کہ بسم اللہ پڑھ کر تیر مارا ہو۔ اور دوسری شرط یہ ہے کہ تیر کا وہ حصہ شکار کو لگا ہو جو دھار دار ہو۔ اگر وہ حصہ لگا جو دھار دار نہیں ہے اور مر گیا تو شکار حلال نہیں ہوگا۔ کیونکہ یہ موقوفہ ہو گیا جو آیت میں حرام ہے۔ اور تیسری شرط یہ ہے کہ شکار کا کوئی حصہ زخمی بھی ہوا ہو۔ ان سب کے دلائل بعد میں آئیں گے۔
ا معلم : سکھایا ہوا ہو، الجوارح : جارحہ سے مشتق ہے زخمی کرنے والا۔ الفھد : چیتا، بازی : ایک قسم کا شکار کرنے والا پرندہ ۔ [۲۵۸۱] (۲) اور کتے کا سکھانا یہ ہے کہ تین مرتبہ کھانا چھوڑ دے اور بازی کی تعلیم یہ ہے کہ واپس لوٹ جائے اگر اس کو بلائے۔
Al-Sharh al-Thamiri vol. 4. Book of Hunting. [25] (2) And the training of the dog is that it leaves off eating three times, and the training of the falcon is that it returns when called. From these trained ones, hunting is permissible. The detail of hunting is that hunting is done in three ways: (1) By means of predatory animals like the dog, cheetah. For hunting with them there are three conditions: first, the dog must be trained. The method of training a dog is that it catches game three times and does not eat its skin, flesh, or bones, but leaves it for its owner; then in the view of Shariah, the dog is considered trained. The method of training all predatory animals is the same. Second condition: the animal is released with Bismillah. Third condition: the predatory animal does not eat from the game after catching it. In such a case, if the animal catches and the game dies before being slaughtered, that game is halal. If the game was alive and the owner had the opportunity to slaughter it but did not, then it is not halal. If there was no opportunity to slaughter and the game died, then it is halal. So if the predatory animal eats from the game after catching it, then that game is not halal for the owner. And in one narration, it is that it must have wounded the game somewhere, which is of the level of forced slaughter and not of the level of strangulation. The second method of hunting is by bird: for example falcon, shikra, etc. For that there are three conditions: first, the bird must be trained. The method of training a bird is that when released it goes for the game and when called back it stops. Doing this three times makes the bird trained in the view of Shariah. It is not based on eating or not eating like the dog. The reason is that the bird is a wild animal by nature, so it comes repeatedly when called and leaves its natural wildness; that is the sign of its training. The dog is a domestic animal that wanders around people. However, it tries to eat after catching the game, so if it leaves the natural habit and does not eat for the owner three times, that is the sign of its being trained. Second condition: release it with Bismillah on the hunt. Now if it eats from the game, it is still halal for the owner. However, if after the game comes into hand, there is an opportunity to slaughter and he does not do so, then it is not halal for the owner. If there was no opportunity to slaughter and the game died, then the game is halal. According to one narration, the third condition is that it must have wounded somewhere, because the verse says 'wa ma 'allamtum min al-jawarih', and jawarih means that which wounds. The third method of hunting is by arrow or gun. For that there are three conditions: first, the arrow is shot with Bismillah. Second condition: the part of the arrow that strikes must be sharp. If the non-sharp part strikes and the game dies, the game is not halal, because it becomes a muwaqqidhah (killed by blunt force) which is haram in the verse. Third condition: some part of the game must be wounded. The proofs for all these will come later. al-Mu'allim: trained. al-Jawarih: derived from jarh, meaning wounding. al-Fahd: cheetah. al-Bazi: a type of hunting bird. [2581] (2) And the training of a dog is that it leaves eating three times, and the training of a falcon is that it returns when called.
Source pages p. 12

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion on hunting by defining what constitutes a 'trained' (mu'allam) animal, then elaborates three distinct methods of hunting with their respective conditions. The passage begins by stating that a dog is considered trained if it refrains from eating the game on three consecutive occasions. A falcon is considered trained if it returns when called. The commentary then explains that hunting is done in three ways: with predatory animals, with birds of prey, and with arrows/guns. For predatory animals (dogs, cheetahs), three conditions are required: (1) the animal is trained, (2) it is released with Bismillah, (3) it does not eat from the catch. The training method for dogs is that on three occasions it catches game but does not consume it; this is also the standard for all predatory animals. If the animal catches and the game dies before the hunter can slaughter it, it is halal. If the hunter reaches the game alive and has the ability to slaughter it but does not, the game becomes impermissible. If the predator eats from the catch, the game is haram. A separate narration adds that the predator must wound the game (making it like an emergency slaughter) rather than strangling it. For birds of prey (falcon, shikra), the training criterion is different: the bird must respond to the call by returning when called, demonstrated three times. Unlike a dog, a bird's training is not measured by not eating the catch; birds are naturally wild and training is shown by obedience to return. For birds, if the bird eats from the catch, the game remains halal, contrary to the rule with dogs. However, if the hunter has opportunity to slaughter and does not, the game becomes impermissible. For arrows/guns, three conditions are: (1) Bismillah is recited when shooting, (2) the arrow hits with a sharp part (blunt force kills are considered muwaqqidhah, which is haram by analogy to the hadith of mi'rad), (3) the game must be wounded (similar to the requirement for predatory animals). The passage concludes with a glossary of key terms: mu'allim (trained), jawarih (wounding animals), fahd (cheetah), bazi (a type of falcon). It then repeats the definition of training for dogs and falcons in Urdu. The author notes that detailed proofs will follow later. The Hanafi school follows these detailed conditions, with differences noted between the training of dogs and birds based on their natures and the relevant texts.

Key Terms
تعليم الكلب (taʿlīm al-kalb): The process of training a hunting dog to refrain from eating the game; established by the dog not eating the catch on three consecutive occasions.
تعليم البازي (taʿlīm al-bāzī): Training a falcon (or other bird of prey) to return when called; tested by three times of responding to the call after being released for the hunt.
الموقوفة (al-mawqūfah): An animal killed by a blunt blow (like the blunt side of an arrow), considered carrion (maytah) and therefore haram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A hunter uses a trained dog to catch a rabbit. The dog catches the rabbit, but the hunter realizes he forgot to say Bismillah when releasing the dog. According to the Hanafi school, is the rabbit halal?
A) Yes, because the dog is trained and did not eat.
B) No, because Bismillah is a required condition for hunting.
C) Yes, because the hunter can say Bismillah retroactively.
D) No, because the dog must also be released by a Muslim.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a dog is trained if it leaves food three times; a falcon is trained if it returns when called; and the conditions for halal hunting include Bismillah, no eating by the animal (for dogs), and a sharp strike (for projectiles).

Rulings on Hunting with Trained Animals: Prey Found Alive and When the Dog Eats
Explains rulings for hunting with dogs/falcons and when prey is found alive

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on prey caught by a trained dog or falcon when the animal eats from the prey, and explain the obligation to slaughter prey if found alive, supported by dalil from Quran and hadith.

Core Idea
If prey is found alive, it must be slaughtered; otherwise it is carrion. The dog eating does not make it haram.

In this lesson, we explore two key rulings from Kitab al-Sayd (the book of hunting). The first addresses a common concern: what if the trained dog or falcon eats from the prey it caught? The second addresses the scenario where the hunter reaches the prey while it is still alive. Both rulings are grounded in clear proofs from the Quran and Sunnah, and understanding them avoids common misunderstandings about halal and haram in hunting.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
State the specific act under discussion: hunting with a trained dog or bird of prey. Determine the overall hukm (mubah) and the sub-rulings: (a) if the animal eats from the prey, the prey remains halal; (b) if the prey is found alive, slaughter becomes wajib.
Focus on the two specific rulings, not the general permissibility.
2
Locate the dalil
Identify the primary proofs cited in the text: Quran 5:3 (exception for what you slaughter) and the hadith of Adi ibn Hatim (if found alive, slaughter; if found dead and not eaten, eat).
The Quranic verse is the foundational proof; the hadith clarifies the application.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the Quranic phrase 'except what you slaughter' (illa ma dhakkaytum) indicates that when the predator has eaten from the prey, the prey can still be halal if it is slaughtered (or was killed by the dog's wound). The hadith distinguishes between prey found alive (must slaughter) and prey found dead with no eating (can eat).
The exception proves the general rule: that which a beast eats is normally haram, unless you are able to slaughter it.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Recognize that Imam al-Shafi'i holds that if the dog eats from the prey, it becomes carrion. The Hanafi school differs, relying on the Quranic exception and the hadith.
This ikhtilaf is a legitimate difference based on interpretation of the same texts.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi within the school, supported by the stronger apparent meaning of the texts. The key practical consequence: if a hunter finds the prey alive, he must slaughter it immediately; otherwise it is haram.
The ruling applies to all trained predatory animals, including falcons (bazi).

الكلب او الفهد لم يوكل وان اكل منه البازى أكل
وان ادرك المرسل الصيد حيا وجب عليه ان يذكّيه ان ترك تذكيته حتى مات لم يوكل
معلوم ہوا کہ باز اور پرندہ شکار میں سے کھالے تب بھی شکار حلال ہے۔ وت باز سے مراد تمام شکاری پرندے ہیں۔
(۲۵۸۴) (۵) اگر چھوڑنے والے نے شکار کو زندہ پایا تو اس پر واجب ہے کہ اس کو ذبح کرے۔ اگر اس کے ذبیح کو چھوڑ دیا یہاں تک کہ مرگیا کو تو نہیں کھایا جائے گا۔
کتا یا بازیا تیر چھوڑنے والے نے شکار کو زندہ پایا تو اس کو فورا ذبح کرنا چاہئے تب شکار حلال ہوگا۔ لیکن ستی کی اور ذبح نہیں کیا اور شکار مر گیا تو اب حلال نہیں ہو گا۔
ے کتے کا پھاڑ نا یا باز کا پھاڑنا یا تیر لگنے سے زخمی ہو جانے سے مر جائے تو اس کو ذبح اضطراری قرار دے کر حلال کر دیا گیا ہے۔ لیکن یہ حلت اس وقت تک ہے جبکہ اصل ذبح پر قادر نہ ہو۔ لیکن یہاں تو شکار کو زندہ پایا اور اصل ذبح پر قدرت ہے پھر بھی اصل شرعی ذبیح نہیں کیا اور مرگیا تو حلال نہیں ہو گا (۲) آیت میں ہے۔ وما اكل السبع الا ما ذكيتم (الف) ( آیت ۳ سورة المائدة (۵) اس آیت میں ہے کہ پھاڑ کھانے والا جانور پھاڑ دے تو ذبح کرنے کے بعد حلال ہے (۳) حدیث میں بھی اشارہ ہے۔ عن عدی بن حاتم قال قال رسول الله الله منه اذا ارسلت کلبک فاذکر اسم الله فان امسک علیک فادركته حیا فاذبحه وان ادركته قد قتل ولم يأكل م فكله (ب) (مسلم شریف، باب الصيد بالكلاب المعلمة ص ۱۴۵ نمبر ۴۹۸۱/۱۹۲۹ (۴) عن قتادة قال ان اخذ کلبک صيدا فانتزعته منه وهو حى فمات في يدك قبل ان تذكيه فلا تأكله (ج) (مصنف عبد الرزاق، باب صید الجارح وهل ترسل کلاب الصيد على الجيف، ج رابع ، ص ۴۷۲، نمبر ۸۵۰۵ / مصنف ابن ابی شیبه ۸ الرجل یا خذ الصید و به رمق ما قالوا فی ذلک و ما جاء فيه؟ ج رابع ، ص ۲۴۴ نمبر ۱۹۶۲۵) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ جانور میں رمق باقی ہو اور ذبح نہیں کیا تو حلال نہیں ہے۔
The dog or leopard: it is not eaten, but if the falcon eats from it, it is eaten. And if the sender finds the prey alive, it is obligatory upon him to slaughter it; if he leaves slaughter until it dies, it is not eaten. It is known that if the falcon or bird eats from the prey, even then the prey is halal. And 'falcon' refers to all hunting birds. (2584) (5) If the sender finds the prey alive, it is obligatory upon him to slaughter it. If he leaves its slaughter until it dies, it will not be eaten. For the dog or falcon or arrow, if the sender finds the prey alive, he should immediately slaughter it; then the prey will be halal. But if he does not slaughter and the prey dies, then it will not be halal. The tearing of the dog or falcon or wounding by the arrow causing death is considered emergency slaughter and made halal. But this permission is only valid when one is not able to perform regular slaughter. However, here the prey was found alive and ability to slaughter exists, yet he did not perform the proper religious slaughter and it died, so it will not be halal. (2) The verse says: 'And what a wild beast has eaten, except what you slaughter' (Surah al-Ma'idah 5:3). In this verse, it says that after the tearing of a predatory animal, it is halal after slaughter. (3) There is also an indication in the hadith: From Adi ibn Hatim, he said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'If you send your dog and mention the name of Allah, and it catches for you, and you find it alive, then slaughter it. And if you find it dead and it has not eaten from it, then eat it.' (Muslim, Bab al-Sayd bi al-Kilab al-Mu'allamah, p. 145, no. 4981/1929) (4) From Qatadah, he said: 'If your dog catches game and you take it from it while it is alive, and it dies in your hand before you slaughter it, then do not eat it.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, Bab Sayd al-Jarih, vol. 4, p. 472, no. 8505; Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, vol. 4, p. 244, no. 19625) From this narration, it is known that if the animal still has life and one does not slaughter it, it is not halal.
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This lesson presents two rulings from Kitab al-Sayd. The first ruling: if a trained dog or leopard (or falcon) eats from the prey, the prey is still halal because the animal's eating does not make it carrion as long as the animal was killed by the dog's wound or the falcon's tear. The second ruling: if the hunter reaches the prey while it is still alive, he must immediately slaughter it; otherwise, if it dies without slaughter, it becomes carrion and is haram. The commentator explains that the permission for 'emergency slaughter' (dhabh idtirari) through the dog's tearing or arrow's wound applies only when one cannot perform regular slaughter. The ruling is supported by Quran 5:3 and a hadith from Adi ibn Hatim, which distinguishes between prey found dead (with no eating from it) and prey found alive (must be slaughtered).

Key Terms
ذكَی (dhakka): To slaughter according to Islamic ritual; to make halal by proper slaughter.
بازى (bāzī): A falcon or any bird of prey trained for hunting.
ذبح اضطراری (dhabh idtirari): Emergency slaughter; the killing of an animal by a trained predatory animal's wound, which renders the meat halal if one cannot perform regular slaughter.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a hunter finds the prey alive after his dog catches it, what must he do?
A) He may let it die without slaughter and still eat it.
B) He must slaughter it immediately; otherwise, it becomes haram.
C) He can leave it and the dog's catching makes it halal regardless.
D) He must set it free.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, prey killed by a trained animal is halal even if the animal eats from it, but if the prey is found alive, it must be slaughtered immediately or it becomes carrion.

Prey Strangled by Dog: Ruling and Intra-Hanafi Difference
Intra-Hanafi dispute on dog-strangled prey

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the relied-upon Hanafi ruling on prey killed by a dog without wounding and explain the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on this issue.

Core Idea
Prey killed by a dog without wounding is not halal; it falls under the forbidden categories of munkhaniqah and mawqudhah.

Hunting with trained dogs is generally permitted in the Hanafi school, but a specific condition applies: the dog must wound the prey and cause blood to flow. If the dog kills by strangulation without any wound, a dispute arises within the school. This lesson examines the relied-upon ruling and the alternative view from Imam Abu Hanifa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the relied-upon ruling
The scenario is a trained dog that kills prey by strangulation without causing any wound or blood flow. The relied-upon Hanafi position, from the matn and commentator, is that this prey is haram and cannot be eaten.
This is the mufta bihi view.
2
Examine the Quranic proof
The proof is from Quran 5:3, which explicitly forbids 'al-munkhaniqah' (strangled) and 'al-mawqudhah' (beaten to death). The dog's action without wounding is analogous to beating, so the prey falls under these categories.
The verse is qat'i in transmission but zanni in dalalah here.
3
Understand the linguistic argument from 'jawarih'
The word 'jawarih' in Quran 5:4 (hunting animals) literally means 'tearing animals'. This implies that the prey must be torn/wounded for it to be halal. If the dog does not tear, the condition is not met.
This strengthens the requirement for wounding.
4
Recognize the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
There is a second narration from Imam Abu Hanifa that even without wounding, the prey is halal. This view is not the relied-upon one; the Zahir al-Riwayah and later authorities prefer the haram ruling.
The difference is practical: whether one may eat such prey.
5
Determine the practical consequence
In practice, a hunter must ensure the dog wounds the prey and blood flows. If the prey is found dead without wounds, it is treated as carrion and cannot be consumed.
This is the mufta bihi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان خنقه الكلب ولم يجرحه لم يوكل
[۲۵۸۵] (۶) أگر کتے نے شکار کا گلا گھونٹ دیا اور زخمی نہیں کیا تو نہیں کھایا جائے گا۔
کتے نے شکار کو پکڑا اور استناد بوچا کہ شکار مرگیا لیکن کسی جگہ زخمی نہیں کیا اور نہ خون نکلا تو یہ شکار حلال نہیں ہے۔
ذبح اضطراری کے لئے ضروری ہے کہ جسم کے کسی حصے سے خون نکلے، یہاں تو کہیں سے خون نہیں نکلا اس لئے آیت کے مطابق یہ منخنقہ اور موقوفہ ہے۔ یعنی گلا گھونٹا ہو یا د بوچ کر چورا کیا ہوا ہو گیا جو حرام ہے۔ آیت یہ ہے حرمت عليكم الميتة والدم ولحم الخنزير وما اهل لغير الله به والمنخنقة والموقوذة والمترديه والنطيحة وما اكل السبع الا ما ذكيتم وما ذبح على النصب (الف) ( آیت ۳ سورۃ المائدۃ (۵) اس آیت میں گلا گھونٹا ہوا اور دبوچ کر چور کئے ہوئے کو حرام قرار دیا ہے۔ اور کتے نے دبوچ کر چور کیا ہے اس لئے حرام ہو گیا (۲) و ما علمتم من الجوارح ( آیت ۴ سورۃ المائدة) سے بھی اندازہ ہوتا ہے کہ پھاڑے تب حلال ہوگا ورنہ نہیں۔ کیونکہ اس میں لفظ جوارح ہے جس کا معنی پھاڑتا ہے۔
فانی امام ابو حنيفہ کی دوسری روایت یہ ہے کہ زخمی نہ کرے تب بھی شکار حلال ہے۔
And if the dog strangles it and does not wound it, it is not eaten.
[2585] (6) If the dog strangled the prey and did not wound it, it will not be eaten. The dog caught the prey and gripped it such that the prey died, but it did not wound it anywhere and no blood came out; this prey is not halal. For emergency slaughter, it is necessary that blood flows from some part of the body; here, blood did not flow from anywhere, so according to the verse, this is 'strangled' (munkhaniqah) and 'beaten' (mawqudhah), i.e., strangled or beaten to death, which is haram. The verse is: 'Forbidden to you are carrion, blood, the flesh of swine, and what was slaughtered for other than Allah, and the strangled, and the beaten to death, and the fallen, and the gored, and what a wild beast has eaten, except what you slaughter, and what is sacrificed on altars' (Surah al-Ma'idah 5:3). In this verse, the strangled and the beaten are declared haram. And the dog has beaten it to death, so it became haram. (2) And from 'what you have taught of hunting animals' (Surah al-Ma'idah 5:4), it is also understood that it is halal only if it tears, otherwise not, because the word 'al-jawarih' means 'tearing'. According to the second narration of Imam Abu Hanifa, even if it does not wound, the prey is still halal.
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute. The relied-upon position (from the matn) is that if the dog kills by strangulation without wounding, the prey is not halal because it falls under the category of 'munkhaniqah' (strangled) and 'mawqudhah' (beaten), mentioned in Quran 5:3 as forbidden. The reason is that emergency slaughter (dhabh idtirari) requires blood to flow from the wound; here, no blood flows. However, there is a second narration from Imam Abu Hanifa that even without wounding, the prey is halal. The commentator favors the first view, citing the verse and the linguistic meaning of 'al-jawarih' (animals that tear).

Key Terms
منخنقة (munkhaniqah): An animal that dies by strangulation without bleeding.
موقوذة (mawqudhah): An animal killed by a blow with a stick or similar without bleeding.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The prey is halal because the dog is trained.
B) The prey is halal according to a second narration from Abu Hanifa.
C) The prey is not halal because it falls under 'munkhaniqah' (strangled) which is haram.
D) The prey is halal only if the hunter witnesses the killing.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, for prey to be halal when killed by a trained dog, the dog must wound the prey and cause blood to flow; otherwise, it is considered carrion and haram.

When a Non-Trained or Magian Dog Joins the Hunt
Explains the effect of another dog joining the hunt

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on prey when an untrained dog joins and explain the dalil from the hadith.

Core Idea
If another dog joins the hunt without Basmalah, the prey is forbidden because the killer is uncertain.

Hunting with trained dogs is permitted in Islam, but strict conditions apply. This lesson examines a common scenario: what happens if an untrained dog, or a dog belonging to a Magian or Christian without proper Basmalah, joins the kill? The Hanafi school relies on a clear hadith to rule that such a catch is not halal.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling
Identify the act (hunting with a trained dog) and the specific situation (another dog joins). State the hukm: the prey is not eaten (haram).
The ruling applies regardless of whether the hunter's dog is trained.
2
Identify the proof
The author cites the hadith of 'Adi ibn Hatim. Locate the explicit prohibition: 'Do not eat, for you have said Bismillah on your dog and not on the other.'
The hadith is found in Bukhari and Muslim.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'لا تأكل' indicates prohibition. The reasoning (ta'lil) is that the Basmalah was only recited on one dog; the other dog's involvement introduces uncertainty about which dog killed.
Uncertainty in the cause of death makes the prey impermissible.
4
Note the extension to Magian and Christian dogs
The text extends the ruling to dogs of Magians and Christians, even if the owner recites Basmalah, because their recitation is not considered valid in this context.
This is a specific Hanafi position; other schools differ.
5
Contrast with other schools
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that if the trained dog alone killed, the prey is halal even if another dog joins. The Hanafi school requires certainty that only the trained dog killed.
The practical difference is the strictness of the requirement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

[۲۵۸۶] (۷) أگر اس کے کتے کے ساتھ غیر معلم کتایا مجوسی کا کتا یا ایسا کتا جس پر بسم اللہ نہ پڑھا گیا ہو شریک ہو گیا تو نہیں کھایا جائے گا۔ حدیث میں ہے کہ غیر معلم یا ایسا کتا جس پر بسم اللہ نہ پڑھا گیا ہو شریک ہو جائے تو اس کار کو مت کھاؤ۔ کیونکہ کیا معلوم کہ کس کتے نے قتل کیا ہے۔ حدیث میں ہے۔ سمعت عدی بن حاتم ... قلت ارسل کلبی فاجد معه كلبا آخر ؟ قال لا تأکل فانک انما سمیت علی کلبک ولم تسم على الآخر (ب) ( بخاری شریف، باب صید ا معروض ص ۸۲۳ نمبر ۵۴۷۶ر مسلم شریف، باب الصيد بالكلاب المعلمة والرمی ص ۱۴۵ نمبر ۴۹۷۴/۱۹۲۹) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ دوسرا کتا شریک ہو جائے تو نہ کھائے۔ مجوسی اور نصرانی کا کتا چونکہ بغیر بسم اللہ کے ہیں۔ اس پر نصرانی بسم اللہ پڑھے تب بھی اس کا اعتبار نہیں ہے اس لئے اس کے شریک ہونے سے بھی نہ کھائے۔
And if a non-trained dog, or a Magian dog, or a dog on which the name of Allah was not mentioned joins, it is not eaten.
[2586] (7) If a non-trained dog, or a Magian dog, or a dog on which Bismillah was not recited joins with his dog, it will not be eaten. In the hadith: A non-trained dog or a dog on which Bismillah was not recited joins, then do not eat it because it is not known which dog killed it. The hadith: I heard 'Adi ibn Hatim... I said: I send my dog and find another dog with it? He said: Do not eat, for you have said Bismillah on your dog and not on the other. (Bukhari, Bab Sayd al-Ma'rud, p. 823, no. 5476; Muslim, Bab al-Sayd bi al-Kilab al-Mu'allamah, p. 145, no. 4974/1929). From this hadith, it is known that if another dog joins, do not eat. The dog of a Magian or Christian, since they are without Bismillah, even if the Christian says Bismillah, it is not considered, so do not eat if it joins.
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This ruling addresses when an untrained dog (kalb ghayr mu'allam) or a dog belonging to a Magian (fire-worshipper) or any dog on which the name of Allah was not recited joins the hunter's trained dog. The prey is not halal because it is uncertain which dog actually killed it. The hadith from 'Adi ibn Hatim makes this clear: the hunter only recited Basmalah on his own dog, so the participation of another dog without Basmalah renders the prey impermissible. The commentary further explains that even if a Christian says Basmalah, it is not valid according to Hanafi, so the prey remains forbidden.

Key Terms
كلب غير معلم (kalb ghayr mu'allam): A dog that has not been trained for hunting following the prescribed method.
مجوسي (majūsī): A Magian/Zoroastrian; their dog's catch is not halal even if they recite Basmalah?

D) The prey is halal if the non-trained dog is a dog of a Christian.

Key Takeaway
The presence of any dog without Basmalah in the kill makes the prey haram due to uncertainty of the killer.

Conditions for Halal Hunting with an Arrow
Explains conditions for hunting with arrow and hadith proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi conditions for halal hunting with an arrow and apply them to distinguish permissible from impermissible cases.

Core Idea
A hunted animal is halal only if the arrow pierces and wounds it, not if it kills by crushing.

Hunting with arrows is a classic scenario in fiqh that tests our understanding of the conditions for halal slaughter. In this lesson, we examine a ruling from the Hanafi school that sets three precise conditions for eating game struck by an arrow. The key distinction comes from a hadith where the Prophet ﷺ differentiates between an arrow that pierces (halal) and one that strikes with its side (haram). By mastering these conditions, you will be able to correctly evaluate hunting scenarios in light of Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The ruling concerns the permissibility of eating game hunted with an arrow. The basic ruling is mubah (permissible) when the three conditions are met. If any condition is missing, the meat becomes haram.
Remember that the default ruling for hunting is permissibility, but it is conditioned.
2
State the three conditions from the text
The text explicitly mentions three conditions: (1) reciting Bismillah at the time of shooting, (2) the arrow must wound the prey (pierce and cause blood flow), (3) the prey must die before the hunter reaches it alive. If found alive, it must be slaughtered properly.
The second condition is the most distinctive: the arrow must 'kharaqa' (pierce), not just kill by blunt force.
3
Analyze the hadith proof
The hadith of 'Adi ibn Hatim quotes the Prophet ﷺ saying: 'Eat what it pierces, and what it hits with its side, do not eat.' The word 'kharaqa' (pierces) is the operative term that justifies the wounding condition. The word 'bī'ardihi' (with its side) indicates killing by crushing, which is not halal.
This hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but its meaning is clear (qat'i al-dalal). The Hanafi school relies on it.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that any projectile that kills the prey is halal as long as the hunter intended and said Basmalah, even if the animal is not wounded. The Hanafi school requires wounding as a condition, based on the hadith distinction.
The practical difference: under Shafi'i, a blunt arrow that kills by impact is halal; under Hanafi, it is haram.
5
Apply the conditions to a scenario
Example: A hunter shoots an arrow that hits a deer with its broad side, crushing its skull, and the deer dies instantly. The hunter had recited Bismillah. According to the Hanafi school, this is not halal because the arrow did not pierce. The hunter must not eat the deer.
If the arrow had pierced the deer's chest and drawn blood, it would be halal, even if the deer died before being reached.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا رمى الرجل سهما الى صيد فسمى الله تعالى عند الرمي أكل ما اصابه اذا جرحه السهم فمات وان
[۲۵۸۷] (۸) أگر آدمی نے شکار پر تیر پھینکا اور تیر پھینکتے وقت بسم اللہ پڑھا تو جس کو لگا وہ کھایا جائے گا اگر تیر اس کو زخمی کر دے اور مر جائے۔ اور اگر شکار زندہ پایا تو اس کو ذبح کرے۔ پس اگر ذبح کرنا چھوڑ دے تو نہیں کھایا جائے گا۔ اوپر تیر سے شکار کرنے کی تین شرطیں بیان کی تھیں ۔ ایک تو یہ کہ بسم اللہ پڑھ کر تیر پھینکا ہو۔ اگر بغیر بسم اللہ کے تیر پھینکا تو شکار حلال نہیں ہے۔ دوسری شرط یہ ہے کہ شکار زخمی ہوا ہوتا کہ ذیح اضطراری ہو جائے، بھینچ کر کے چورا ہوا ہو تو حلال نہیں ۔ اور تیسری شرط یہ ہے کہ ہاتھ میں آنے سے پہلے مر چکا ہو۔ اگر ہاتھ میں آتے وقت زندہ تھا تو ذبح کرنا ہوگا۔ اگر ذبح نہیں کیا اور مر گیا تو اب حلال نہیں ہے۔ حدیث میں ہے۔ عن عدی بن حاتم ؛؛؛ قلت انا نرمى بالمعراض ؟ قال كل ما خرق وما اصاب بعرضه فلا تأكل (ج) (بخاری شریف ، باب ما اصاب المعراض بعرضه ص ۸۲۳ نمبر ٫۵۴۷۷ مسلم شریف ، باب الصيد بالكلاب المعلمة والرمی ص ۱۴۵ نمبر
And if a man shoots an arrow at game and mentions the name of Allah at the time of shooting, he eats what it hits if the arrow wounds it and it dies. And if he finds the prey alive, he should slaughter it. Then if he abandons slaughter, it will not be eaten.
[2587] (8) If a man threw an arrow at game and at the time of throwing he recited Bismillah, then whatever it hits will be eaten if the arrow wounds it and it dies. And if the prey is found alive, he should slaughter it. So if he leaves slaughter, it will not be eaten. Above, three conditions for hunting with an arrow were mentioned: First, that he threw the arrow reciting Bismillah. If he threw without Bismillah, the prey is not halal. Second condition: that the prey must be wounded so that it becomes emergency slaughter; if it is crushed or broken, it is not halal. Third condition: that it dies before reaching the hand. If it was alive when reaching the hand, it must be slaughtered. If he does not slaughter and it dies, then it is not halal. In the hadith: From 'Adi ibn Hatim: I said: I shoot with al-mi'rad? He said: Eat what it pierces, and what it hits with its side, do not eat. (Bukhari, Bab ma asaba al-mi'rad bi 'ardihi, p. 823, no. 5477; Muslim, Bab al-Sayd bi al-Kilab al-Mu'allamah, p. 145)
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This lesson details the conditions for the permissibility of hunting with arrows or similar projectiles. Three conditions are derived: (1) The hunter must recite Basmalah at the time of shooting; otherwise, the prey is haram. (2) The arrow must wound the prey, i.e., penetrate and cause blood flow, so that emergency slaughter (dhabh idtirari) occurs; if the prey is killed by crushing from the arrow's side, it is not halal. (3) The prey must die from the wound before the hunter reaches it alive. If the hunter reaches it alive, he must perform proper Islamic slaughter; failure to do so makes it haram. The hadith from 'Adi ibn Hatim distinguishes between an arrow that pierces (which is allowed) and one that hits with its broad side (which is not allowed, as it kills by crushing).

Key Terms
معراض (mi'rad): An arrow without feathers that can kill by piercing or by striking with its breadth.
خرق (kharaqa): To pierce or penetrate, causing a wound.
عرض (‘ard): The side or breadth of the arrow.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is NOT a condition for hunting with an arrow?
A) The hunter recites Bismillah at the time of shooting.
B) The arrow wounds the prey and causes blood flow.
C) The prey must die before the hunter reaches it alive.
D) The arrow must be shot while the hunter is mounted.

Key Takeaway
The three Hanafi conditions for halal hunting with an arrow are: Basmalah at shooting, the arrow must pierce and wound, and the prey must die before being found alive; otherwise, slaughter is required.

The Two Hanafi Narrations on Game Killed Without Wounding
Ruling with dalil and intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi narrations regarding game killed by a dog without wounding and explain the Quranic evidence for the first narration.

Core Idea
A dog's kill without wounding is haram by analogy to strangled animals, but a second narration from Abu Hanifa permits it.

Hunting with trained dogs is generally permissible in the Hanafi school. However, a specific issue arises when the dog kills the game by strangulation without tearing the flesh. The matn of this lesson declares such game not eaten, citing Quranic verses. Yet, a second narration from Imam Abu Hanifa considers it halal. This lesson unpacks both positions, the evidence, and the nature of the ikhtilaf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Legal Question
Determine the precise scenario: a trained dog kills game by strangling (e.g., clamping the throat) without causing a visible wound. Is the game halal or haram?
The dog is assumed to be trained and the hunter says Bismillah.
2
Extract the First Narration (Matn Ruling)
The matn states: 'خنقه الكلب ولم يجرحه لم يوكل' – if the dog strangles it and does not wound it, it is not eaten. Thus the first narration rules it haram.
This is the position presented as the primary ruling in the text.
3
Analyze the Quranic Evidence for the First Narration
The author cites two verses. Quran 5:3 lists 'al-munkhaniqah' (the strangled) as prohibited; by qiyas, the game strangled by the dog falls under this prohibition. Quran 5:4 uses the word 'jawarih' (tearing beasts), implying that the hunting animal must wound for the game to be halal.
The dalil block confirms thubut = qati (Quran) but dalala = zanni (qiyas).
4
Identify the Second Narration and Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf
The text then states: 'فاني امام ابو حنيفة کی دوسری روایت یہ ہے کہ زخمی نہ کرے تب بھی شکار حلال ہے' – a second narration from Imam Abu Hanifa holds the game halal even without wounding.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf between two transmitted positions of the same Imam.
5
Assess the Authority and Practical Difference
The first narration is likely the relied-upon (Zahir al-Riwayah) position, while the second is nawadir. The mufta bihi is not specified here, but later Hanafi works may resolve. The practical difference: under the first, the game is not eaten; under the second, it is halal.
The madhhab dispute map will organize these details.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
خنقه الكلب ولم يجرحه لم يوكل الخنزير وما اهل لغير الله به والمنخنقة والموقوذة والمترديه والنطيحة وما اكل السبع الا ما ذكيتم وما ذبح على النصب (الف) ( آیت ۳ سورۃ المائدۃ (۵) اس آیت میں گلا گھونٹا ہوا اور دبوچ کر چور کئے ہوئے کو حرام قرار دیا ہے۔ اور کتے نے دبوچ کر چور کیا ہے اس لئے حرام ہو گیا (۲) و ما علمتم من الجوارح ( آیت ۴ سورۃ المائدة) سے بھی اندازہ ہوتا ہے کہ پھاڑے تب حلال ہوگا ورنہ نہیں۔ کیونکہ اس میں لفظ جوارح ہے جس کا معنی پھاڑتا ہے۔ فانی امام ابو حنیفہ کی دوسری روایت یہ ہے کہ زخمی نہ کرے تب بھی شکار حلال ہے۔
If the dog strangles it and does not wound it, it is not eaten. The Quranic verse: 'Carriage, blood, flesh of swine, and what has been dedicated to other than Allah, and the strangled, and the beaten, and the fallen, and the gored, and what a wild beast has eaten — except what you slaughter, and what is sacrificed on altars.' (Surah Al-Ma'idah 5:3). In this verse, strangled and what is killed by clamping are declared haram. And the dog has killed by clamping, so it becomes haram. And from 'And what you have taught of hunting birds and beasts' (Surah Al-Ma'idah 5:4) it is also inferred that if it tears [the game] then it is halal, otherwise not, because the word 'jawarih' means 'that which tears'. And the second narration from Imam Abu Hanifa is that even if it does not wound, the game is still halal.
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling on game killed by a dog that does not wound but strangles. The matn states clearly: it is not eaten. The author then cites the Quranic verse (5:3) listing prohibited animals, including the strangled (al-munkhaniqah). Since the dog kills by strangulation, it falls under this prohibition. The verse about taught hunting dogs (5:4) implies that the dog must 'tear' (jarih), meaning wounding is necessary. However, the text then adds a second narration from Imam Abu Hanifa that the game is halal even without wounding. This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf. The first narration (the relied-upon?) holds that wounding is required; the second considers strangulation sufficient. The commentary does not specify which is mufta bihi, but the matn states the stricter view.

Key Terms
جوارح (jawarih): In this context, hunting dogs and birds that tear the game; the word implies wounding.
المنخنقة (al-munkhaniqah): The strangled animal, prohibited in Quran 5:3.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Quranic evidence cited in the lesson, which verse provides the basis for the condition that the hunting dog must wound the game?
A) Quran 5:3 – the prohibition of strangled animals
B) Quran 5:4 – the word 'jawarih' (tearing beasts)
C) Both A and B
D) Neither

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the relied-upon position is that game killed by a trained dog without wounding is haram, based on Quranic analogy, though a minority narration permits it.

Sharing of Untrained or Magian Dog in Hunting
Ruling on when an untrained or Magian dog joins the hunt

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when an untrained or Magian dog joins a hunt and identify the dalil from the hadith of Adi ibn Hatim.

Core Idea
If another dog joins the hunt, the game is haram because Tasmiyah was not made over that dog.

Hunting with trained dogs is permitted in Islam under strict conditions. One key condition is that the dog must be sent with Tasmiyah (pronouncing Bismillah) and must be trained (mu'allam). But what happens if another dog, untrained or belonging to a non-Muslim, joins in? The famous hadith of Adi ibn Hatim gives the answer: do not eat. In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling and its proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is hunting with a trained dog. The ruling when another dog (untrained, without Tasmiyah, or from a Magian) joins is that the game is haram (not to be eaten).
The text states 'lam yu'kal' (not eaten).
2
Locate the dalil
The dalil is the hadith of Adi ibn Hatim recorded in Bukhari and Muslim, where the Prophet (peace be upon him) explicitly said not to eat if another dog is found with the hunter's dog.
The hadith is ahad but authentic (sahih).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's command 'la ta'kul' (do not eat) indicates prohibition. The reason given is that the hunter only said Bismillah over his own dog, not over the other dog. This establishes that Tasmiyah must be made over every contributing animal.
The hadith text: 'فانک انما سمیت علی کلبک ولم تسم على الآخر'
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school may consider the game halal if it is certain that the trained dog made the kill, arguing that the partner dog does not affect the ruling. However, the Hanafi school holds that the presence of any dog without Tasmiyah creates uncertainty and thus prohibition.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf based on different interpretations of the hadith.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi school relies on the apparent meaning (zahir) of the hadith, which is general and unconditional. Since the hadith does not make exception for cases where the trained dog is the killer, the prohibition stands. This is the mufta bihi position.
The hadith is clear and not overridden by istihsan.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان شارکه کلب غیر معلم او کلب مجوسي او كلب لم يُذكر اسم الله تعالى عليه لم يركل [۲۵۸۶] (۷) اگر اس کے کتے کے ساتھ غیر معلم کتا یا مجوسی کا کتا یا ایسا کتا جس پر بسم اللہ نہ پڑھا گیا ہو شریک ہو گیا تو نہیں کھایا جائے گا۔ حدیث میں ہے کہ غیر معلم یا ایسا کتا جس پر بسم اللہ نہ پڑھا گیا ہو شریک ہو جائے تو اس کار کو مت کھاؤ۔ کیونکہ کیا معلوم کہ کس کتے نے قتل کیا ہے۔ حدیث میں ہے۔ سمعت عدی بن حاتم ... قلت ارسل کلبی فاجد معه كلبا آخر ؟ قال لا تأکل فانک انما سمیت علی کلبک ولم تسم على الآخر (ب) ( بخاری شریف، باب صید ا معروض ص ۸۲۳ نمبر ۵۴۷۶ر مسلم شریف، باب الصيد بالكلاب المعلمة والرمی ص ۱۴۵ نمبر ۴۹۷۴/۱۹۲۹) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ دوسرا کتا شریک ہو جائے تو نہ کھائے۔ مجوسی اور نصرانی کا کتا چونکہ بغیر بسم اللہ کے ہیں۔ اس پر نصرانی بسم اللہ پڑھے تب بھی اس کا اعتبار نہیں ہے اس لئے اس کے شریک ہونے سے بھی نہ کھائے۔
And if a dog that is not trained, or a dog of a Magian, or a dog over which the name of Allah was not mentioned, partners [in the hunt], it is not eaten. [Urdu:] If with his dog, an untrained dog, or a Magian's dog, or a dog over which 'Bismillah' was not recited, joins, then it will not be eaten. There is a hadith: that if an untrained dog or a dog over which 'Bismillah' was not recited joins, then do not eat that game, because it is not known which dog killed it. There is a hadith: 'I heard Adi bin Hatim... I said: I send my dog and find with it another dog? He said: Do not eat, for you said Bismillah over your dog and not over the other.' (Bukhari, Muslim). From this hadith it is understood that if another dog joins, do not eat. The dog of a Magian or Christian is without Bismillah; even if the Christian recites Bismillah, it is not considered, so if such a dog joins, do not eat.
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This ruling addresses a scenario where the hunter's trained dog is joined by another dog that is either untrained, or belongs to a Magian or Christian, or was not sent with Tasmiyah. In such cases, the game is not lawful because it is uncertain which dog actually killed it, and the condition of the hunter's own dog having been sent with Tasmiyah is not fulfilled for the other. The hadith of Adi ibn Hatim explicitly prohibits eating when another dog joins the hunt. The text further states that a Magian's dog is considered 'without Bismillah' because the Magian is not considered to have valid faith; even if a Christian recites Bismillah, it is not valid according to the Hanafi school because of their incorrect belief. Therefore, participation of such a dog renders the game haram.

Key Terms
غير معلم (ghayr mu'allam): A dog that has not been trained to hunt; also implies it will not return or hold the game properly.
مجوسي (majusi): A fire-worshipper; their dog is considered like an untrained dog in terms of Tasmiyah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith cited, what should a hunter do if his dog catches game but another dog has joined it?
A) He may eat it because his dog was sent with Bismillah
B) He should not eat it because he did not say Bismillah over the other dog
C) He should slaughter it and then eat
D) He should feed it to his dog

Key Takeaway
When another dog joins the hunt, the game is haram because Tasmiyah was not made over the second dog, regardless of the original dog's training.

Conditions for Eating Game Shot with an Arrow
Ruling on conditions for eating game shot with arrow

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions for eating game shot with an arrow and apply them to identify when the game is halal or haram.

Core Idea
Three conditions: Tasmiyah at shooting, arrow wounds, game not found alive. If found alive, must slaughter.

The Hanafi school teaches that hunting with a bow and arrow is permissible, but strict conditions apply. This lesson examines the ruling and its proofs from the Quran and Sunnah, ensuring you understand when the game becomes halal and when it does not.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default ruling
The act is shooting game with an arrow. The default ruling is that it is halal only if specific conditions are met.
2
List the three conditions from the matn
From the text: (1) tasmiyah (saying Bismillah) at the moment of shooting, (2) the arrow must wound the game, (3) the game must die before the hunter finds it alive. If found alive, slaughter is required.
The commentary emphasizes that if the arrow does not wound, the game is not considered emergency slaughter (dhabh idtirari).
3
Examine the proof for tasmiyah
The hadith of Abu Tha'laba (Bukhari, Muslim) states: '...and what you hunt with your bow and remember the name of Allah, eat.' The imperative 'fakul' indicates obligation of tasmiyah. Also the Quranic verse 5:4 commands mentioning Allah's name when sending hunting animals.
The analogy is drawn from hunting dogs to bows.
4
Examine the proof for slaughter when found alive
The hadith of Adi ibn Hatim (Muslim) says: 'When you send your dog, mention Allah's name. If it catches for you and you find it alive, slaughter it.' This establishes the duty to slaughter if the game is still alive.
If the hunter fails to slaughter after finding it alive, the game becomes haram.
5
Apply the conditions to a scenario
Given a scenario, check each condition. Example: hunter says Bismillah, arrow wounds the deer, deer dies before being found. Halal. If arrow hits with flat side causing death without wound, not halal because no wound.
Missing any condition makes the game impermissible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا رمى الرجل سهما الى صيد فسمى الله تعالى عند الرمي أكل ما اصابه اذا جرحه السهم فمات وان ادرکه حیا فترك تذكيته لم يؤكل [۲۵۸۸](۹) واذا وقع السهم بالصيد فتحامل حتى غاب عنه ولم يزل في طلبه حتى اصابه ميتا أكل فان قعد عن طلبه ثم اصابه ۱۹۲۹) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ تیر زخمی کرے تو کھا سکتا ہے اور زخمی نہ کرے تو چونکہ ذبیح اضطراری بھی نہیں ہوا اس لئے نہ کھائے۔ اور تیر بسم اللہ پڑھ کر پھینکے اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن ابي ثعلبة الخشني ... وما صدت بقوسک فذكرت اسم الله فکل (الف) ( بخاری شریف، باب صید القوس ص ۸۲۳ نمبر ۵۴۷۸، مسلم شریف ، باب الصيد بالكلاب المعلمة والرمی ص ۱۴۵ نمبر ۴۹۸۲/۱۹۲۹) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ تیر پھینکتے وقت بسم اللہ پڑھے (۲) آیت بھی گزر چکی ہے۔ فكلوا مما امسكن عليكم واذكروا اسم الله عليه ( آیت ۴ سورۃ المائدۃ ۵) اس آبرت، سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ تیر پھینکتے وقت بسم اللہ پڑھے۔ اور زندہ ہاتھ آئے تو ذبح کرے تب حلال ہوگی اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن عدی بن حاتم قال قال لى رسول الله اذا ارسلت کلبک فاذکر اسم الله فان امسک علیک فادركته حيا فاذبحه (ب) (مسلم شریف ، باب الصيد بالكلاب المعلمة والرمی ص ۱۴۵ نمبر ۴۹۸۱/۱۹۲۹ رمصنف عبدالرزاق، باب صید الجارح الخ ج رابع ص ۴۷۲ نمبر ۸۵۰۵) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ زندہ پائے تو اس کو ذبح کرے تب حلال ہوگا۔
And if a man shoots an arrow at game and mentions the name of Allah at the time of shooting, he may eat what it hits if the arrow wounds it and it dies. And if he finds it alive and then leaves off slaughtering it, it is not eaten. [The text then continues on page 17 with:] And if the arrow hits the game and it staggers until it disappears from his sight, and he does not cease pursuing it until he finds it dead, he may eat it. But if he sits down from pursuing it and then finds it, [he may not?] ... From this hadith it is understood that if the arrow wounds, he may eat; if it does not wound, since it did not become a dhabihat idtirari (emergency slaughter), do not eat. And the proof that the arrow must be shot with Tasmiyah is the hadith of Abu Tha'laba: '...and what you hunt with your bow and remember the name of Allah, eat.' (Bukhari, Muslim). From this hadith it is understood that one should say Bismillah at the time of shooting. Also the verse (5:4) 'So eat of what they catch for you and mention the name of Allah upon it' indicates that. And if found alive, one must slaughter; its proof is the hadith of Adi ibn Hatim: 'When you send your dog, mention the name of Allah. If it catches for you and you find it alive, slaughter it.' (Muslim). So if found alive, one must slaughter to make it halal.
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This passage details the conditions for eating game killed by an arrow. The matn states three conditions: (1) Tasmiyah at shooting, (2) the arrow must wound, (3) the game must die before being found alive; if found alive, the hunter must slaughter it, otherwise it is not halal. The commentary explains the reasoning and provides proofs from hadith and Quran. The hadith of Abu Tha'laba establishes the necessity of Tasmiyah at the time of shooting. The verse (5:4) commands mentioning Allah's name when sending hunting dogs or birds, analogically applied to arrows. The hadith of Adi ibn Hatim (about dogs) shows the principle that if the animal is found alive, it requires slaughter. The commentary also mentions that if the arrow does not wound, the game is not halal because it lacks the characteristic of emergency slaughter (dhabh idtirari). The Arabic line 'واذا وقع السهم...' (starting a new rule about the game disappearing) appears here but the commentary directly following is still on the arrow conditions; to avoid confusion, the rule about game disappearing will be covered in the next lesson.

Key Terms
ذبیح اضطراری (dhabihah idtirariyyah): Emergency slaughter caused by the arrow wound; if the arrow wounds, it is considered as if slaughtered.
تسمية (tasmiyah): Uttering the name of Allah (Bismillah) at the time of shooting or slaughtering.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a hunter shoots a game with an arrow, says Bismillah, but finds the animal alive?
A) He may eat it as it is
B) He must slaughter it before eating
C) It is not halal because it was not killed by the arrow
D) He should leave it for the dogs

Key Takeaway
Game shot with an arrow is halal only if three conditions are met: Bismillah at shooting, the arrow wounds, and the game dies before being found alive (or is slaughtered if found alive).

Continuous Pursuit in Hunting: When Lost Game is Halal
Ruling on game hit by arrow and lost, then found dead

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on game that disappears after being hit by an arrow and explain why continuous pursuit is a condition for halal consumption.

Core Idea
Continuous pursuit ensures certainty; stopping creates doubt, making the game haram.

When hunting with arrows, a shooter may lose sight of the game after it is hit. This lesson examines the precise ruling from the Hanafi school: if the hunter never stops searching and finds the game dead, it is halal; if he gives up the search and later finds it, it is not. We will also study the hadith evidence that underpins this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and ruling
The passage describes two scenarios: (1) the arrow hits the game, it staggers away, the hunter continuously pursues and finds it dead → halal. (2) The hunter sits down (stops pursuing) and later finds it dead → not halal.
The key distinction is the continuity of pursuit.
2
Understand the condition of continuous pursuit
Continuous pursuit is not merely a recommended act; it is a condition (shart) for the game to be considered halal. Stopping the pursuit introduces uncertainty about whether the arrow alone caused death.
The commentary emphasizes that stopping creates doubt (shakk) in the cause of death.
3
Examine the dalil
The hadith of Adi ibn Hatim (Bukhari and Muslim) explicitly permits eating if the game is found after a day or two with only the arrow mark, provided it did not fall into water. The commentator also cites the hadith of Abu Tha'laba adding that the game must not be putrid.
These hadith are ahad but considered qat'i in dalala for this specific ruling.
4
Derive the condition from the dalil and commentary
The hadith does not explicitly mention continuous pursuit; the condition is derived by combining the hadith with the principle that certainty (yaqeen) is required for halal. If pursuit stops, the arrow might have struck a mortally wounded animal that then died from another cause, introducing uncertainty.
The Hanafi jurists use istidlal (inference) from the purpose of the law (preserving life and avoiding doubt).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

ذبح کرے تب حلال ہوگا۔ [The page continues with the specific commentary for this ruling:] شکار کو تیر مارا، شکار اس کو برداشت کرتے ہوئے بھا گا اور شکاری کی آنکھوں سے غائب ہو گیا اب وہ مسلسل تلاش کر تار And if the arrow hits the game and it staggers until it disappears from his sight, and he does not cease pursuing it until he finds it dead, he may eat it. But if he sits down from pursuing it and then finds it, [he may not?] ... From this hadith it is understood that if the arrow wounds, he may eat; if it does not wound, since it did not become a dhabihat idtirari (emergency slaughter), do not eat. ... [Then the specific commentary:] If the game is hit by the arrow, it staggers away and disappears from the hunter's sight, and he continuously searches and finds it dead, then he may eat it. And if he sits down from searching and then finds it dead, he may not eat it. There is a hadith: from Adi ibn Hatim from the Prophet: '...If you shoot the game and find it after a day or two with no mark except your arrow, then eat. But if it falls in water, do not eat.' (Bukhari, Muslim). From this hadith it is understood that if it is certain your arrow killed it, even after two days, you may eat as long as it is not putrid. Because in another hadith from Abu Tha'laba: 'If you shoot your arrow and it disappears from you, then you find it, eat it as long as it has not become stinking.' (Muslim). And if he continues searching and finds it dead, he may eat; if he sits down and then finds it dead, he may not eat. The proof is the hadith of Adi: he asked the Prophet about shooting game and tracking its trace after two or three days, then finding it dead with his arrow. He said: Eat if he wishes.
Source pages p. 17

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling for a specific scenario: the arrow hits the game, the game disappears while the hunter pursues continuously, and eventually finds it dead. The matn states: if he pursues without stopping, he may eat; if he stops pursuit, he may not eat. The commentary supports this with two hadiths: one from Adi ibn Hatim allowing eating if the game is found after a day or two with only the hunter's arrow's mark, provided it is not putrid; another from Abu Tha'laba with similar conditions. The key point is that the hunter must be certain the arrow caused the death and must have been in continuous pursuit. If he gives up and later finds it, the uncertainty increases and the game becomes prohibited.

Key Terms
فتحامل (fatahammala): To struggle and stagger away; used for the game after being hit.
قعد عن طلبه (qa'ada an talabihi): He sat down from pursuing; i.e., he stopped and gave up the search.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a hunter shoots a game, it disappears, and he stops searching but later finds it dead with only his arrow mark, what is the Hanafi ruling?
A) It is halal to eat
B) It is not halal to eat
C) It is halal if within two days
D) It is makruh

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, game that disappears after being hit by an arrow is only halal if the hunter pursues continuously until finding it dead; stopping the pursuit makes it haram.
