[2601] (22) And the slaughter of a Muslim and a Kitabi is halal. [2601] (22) The slaughtered animal of a Muslim and a Kitabi is halal. If a Muslim recites Bismillah and slaughters, the animal is halal. Similarly, if a person of the Book, i.e., a Jew or Christian, recites Bismillah and slaughters, the slaughtered animal is halal. In the verse: 'Today I have made permissible for you good things, and the food of those who were given the Scripture is permissible for you, and your food is permissible for them' (Surah al-Ma'idah 5:5). In this verse, the food of those given the Scripture (Jews and Christians) meaning their slaughtered animals, is halal for you. (2) From Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with him) that he said: 'Their food means their slaughtered animals' (Bukhari, Chapter on Slaughter of Ahl al-Kitab..., no. 5508; Bayhaqi, Chapter on Food of Ahl al-Kitab, vol. 9, p. 474, no. 19152). From this narration it is known that the 'food' in the verse refers to their slaughtered animals. European Christians are generally heretics; they are Christians in name only and do not recite Bismillah when slaughtering, which is necessary for Muslims, so caution is required regarding their slaughter. In a narration: Al-Zuhri said: 'There is no harm in the slaughter of the Christian Arabs, but if you hear him invoking other than Allah, do not eat' (Bukhari, Chapter on Slaughter of Ahl al-Kitab..., no. 5508). From this narration it is known that if he invokes other than Allah, do not eat, and from this it is also known that if he does not recite Bismillah, it is not halal. And European Christians do not recite Bismillah at all, so their slaughter is not halal. (3) In a narration: Umar ibn al-Khattab said: 'The Christian Arabs are not people of the Book, and their slaughter is not halal for us, and I will not leave them until they accept Islam or I strike their necks' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Chapter on Slaughter of Arab Christians, vol. 9, p. 478, no. 19169). When the Arab Christians in the time of the Companions were not people of the Book, how can European Christians be Muslims in this time?

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. The matn states that the slaughter of a Muslim and a Kitabi (Jew/Christian) is halal. The Urdu commentary explains that if they recite Bismillah, the meat is halal, citing Quran 5:5 and the interpretation of Ibn Abbas that 'food' means 'slaughter'. It then discusses a practical issue: European Christians are considered heretics and do not recite Bismillah, so their slaughter is not halal. This is supported by the narration of al-Zuhri that if they invoke other than Allah, do not eat, implying that Bismillah is required. The commentary also cites Umar's statement that Arab Christians of his time were not Ahl al-Kitab, suggesting that European Christians today are even less so. Therefore, caution is advised.

Key Terms
ذبيحة (dhabihah): An animal that has been ritually slaughtered.
كتابي (kitabi): A person of the Book (Jew or Christian).
بسم اللہ (Bismillah): The phrase 'In the name of Allah' recited at the time of slaughter.

Slaughter by Apostate, Magian, Idolater, and Muhrim is Not Halal
Ruling on the prohibition of slaughter by four categories

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the permissibility of consuming meat from the slaughter of an apostate, Magian, idolater, and Muhrim, and identify the reason why their slaughter is not halal.

Core Idea
The slaughter of an apostate, Magian, idolater, or Muhrim is haram because they are neither Muslims nor Ahl al-Kitab.

This lesson addresses a specific ruling in fiqh regarding the validity of slaughter (dhabiha) performed by individuals who are not recognized as having the capacity to produce halal meat. The Hanafi school, based on the Qur'an and Sunnah, establishes that only Muslims and Ahl al-Kitab (People of the Book) can perform valid slaughter. Here, we examine four categories—apostate, Magian, idolater, and Muhrim—and why their slaughter is impermissible. The proof is a hadith, though its exact text is not quoted in this passage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Categories and Ruling
List the four categories mentioned: apostate (murtadd), Magian (majusi), idolater (wathani), and Muhrim (one in ihram). The ruling is that their slaughter is not halal and must not be consumed.
The Muhrim is a Muslim in a restricted state, not a disbeliever.
2
Understand the Legal Reasoning
The commentary explains that these individuals are neither Muslims nor Ahl al-Kitab, but disbelievers. Additionally, they do not believe in Bismillah or their recitation is not reliable, and reciting Bismillah is necessary for valid slaughter.
3
Distinguish the Basis for Muhrim
The Muhrim's slaughter is invalid because of the state of ihram, not because of disbelief. A Muhrim is prohibited from hunting and slaughtering during Hajj or Umrah.
This is a separate prohibition from the disbeliever categories.
4
Connect to the Proof
The text cites a hadith as the proof (though the exact words are not provided). The hadith likely states that the slaughter of such individuals is impermissible.
5
Apply the Ruling to Contrast Cases
Contrast with the slaughter of a Jew or Christian (Ahl al-Kitab), which is halal if they recite Bismillah. The four categories in this lesson are excluded from that allowance.
The Hanafi school considers Magians as not Ahl al-Kitab.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

[2602] (23) And do not eat the slaughter of an apostate. [2602] (23) The slaughter of an apostate, Magian, idolater, and Muhrim will not be eaten. These people are neither Muslims nor Ahl al-Kitab; rather they are disbelievers, so their slaughter is not halal. They do not believe in Bismillah, nor is their Bismillah reliable, and reciting Bismillah is necessary, so it will not be halal. (2) Hadith

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (though the hadith text is cut off). The matn states that the slaughter of an apostate (murtadd), Magian (Majusi), idolater (wathani), and Muhrim (one in ihram) is not halal. The Urdu commentary explains that these individuals are not Muslim nor are they Ahl al-Kitab; they are disbelievers. Their slaughter is invalid because they do not believe in Bismillah or their recitation is not reliable, and since reciting Bismillah is a necessary condition for halal slaughter, their meat is not permissible. The mention of 'Hadith' indicates a prophetic proof, but the text ends abruptly.

Key Terms

مجوسي (majusi): Magian, follower of Zoroastrianism.
محرم (muhrim): One in the state of ihram for Hajj or Umrah.

Ruling on Slaughter of Majusi, Apostate, and Idol Worshipper
Ruling with proof from hadith and qiyas extension.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the slaughter of a Majusi, an apostate, and an idol worshipper, and identify the primary proof (hadith) and the analogical reasoning (qiyas) used to extend the ruling.

Core Idea
Slaughter of a Majusi is haram by explicit hadith; apostate and idol worshipper follow by qiyas.

This passage presents a clear ruling with proof: eating meat from an animal slaughtered by a Majusi (Zoroastrian) is prohibited. The evidence is a hadith in which the Prophet stipulates that the Magians of Hajar who accept jizyah must not have their slaughtered animals eaten. The author then extends this ruling by analogy to apostates (murtadd) and idol worshippers (wathani), as they share the attribute of not being Ahl al-Kitab. Understanding this ruling helps distinguish permissible from forbidden sources of meat in daily life.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The passage states the ruling that the slaughter of a Majusi, an idol worshipper, and a muhrim (here, the muhrim is a minor issue; the focus is on Majusi and the qiyas extension) is prohibited. First, note the hukm: not halal (haram).
2
Locate the primary dalil
The author cites a hadith from al-Hasan ibn Muhammad ibn al-Hanafiyyah, reported by al-Bayhaqi and al-Daraqutni. The Prophet wrote to the Magians of Hajar, offering Islam, and for those who refused, jizyah was imposed on condition that their slaughtered animal would not be eaten.
The hadith is ahad (single-chain) with zanni thubut and dalala, but it is accepted in the Hanafi school.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The operative phrase is 'ala alla tu'kala dhabihah' (on condition that their slaughtered animal will not be eaten). This explicit stipulation indicates prohibition.
The condition is directly linked to the ruling: prohibition of eating.
4
Trace the qiyas extension
The author performs qiyas: the asl is the Majusi, the hukm is that his slaughter is not halal, the illa is that he is not Ahl al-Kitab. The far' is the apostate and idol worshipper, who share the same illa. Thus the ruling is extended.
The qiyas is jaliyyah (clear analogy) with tahrir al-manat extraction.
5
Confirm the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is that the slaughter of a Majusi, apostate, and idol worshipper is not halal. This is based on the hadith and the qiyas.
No intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf is noted; the ruling is well-established.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمجوسي والوثنى والمحرم.
۱۹
كتاب الصيد
للبيبقى ، باب
مرسل میں ہے۔ عن الحسن بن محمد بن الحنفية قال كتب رسول الله الى مجوس هجر يعرض عليهم الاسلام فمن اسلم قبل منه ومن ابي ضربت علهم الجزية على ان لا توكل ذبيحة ولا تنكح لهم امرأة (الف) (سنن ) ما جاء فی ذبحته المجوسی ج تاسع ص ۲۷۸ نمبر ۱۹۱۷۱ار دار قطنی ، کتاب الاشربة ج رابع ص ۱۹۷ نمبر ۴۷۵۵) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ مجوسی کا ذبیحہ جائز نہیں ہے اور اسی پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے مرتد اور بت پرست کا ذبیحہ حلال نہیں ہے۔

حاشیہ : (الف) حضور نے ہجر کے مجوس کے بارے میں لکھوایا کہ ان پر اسلام پیش کیا جائے گا، جو ان میں سے اسلام لے آئے ان سے قبول کیا جائے گا اور جوانکار کرے ان پر جز یہ تعین کیا جائے گا اس شرط پر کہ ان کا ذبیحہ نہیں کھایا جائے گا اور نہ ان کی عورتوں سے نکاح کیا جائے گا
And the Magian, the idol worshipper, and the Muhrim. 19 Book of Hunting. For al-Bayhaqi, Chapter: Mursal: From al-Hasan ibn Muhammad ibn al-Hanafiyyah, he said: The Messenger of Allah wrote to the Magians of Hajar, presenting Islam to them. So whoever accepted Islam, it was accepted from him, and whoever refused, jizyah was imposed on them on the condition that their slaughtered animal would not be eaten and their women would not be married. (Al-Sunan: What came regarding the slaughter of the Magian, vol. 9, p. 278, no. 19171; al-Daraqutni, Book of Drinks, vol. 4, p. 197, no. 4755) From this narration it is known that the slaughter of a Magian is not permissible, and by analogy, the slaughter of an apostate and an idol worshipper is not halal.

Footnote (a): The Prophet wrote concerning the Magians of Hajar that Islam would be presented to them; whoever among them accepted Islam would be accepted from him, and whoever refused would have jizyah imposed on them on the condition that their slaughtered animal would not be eaten and their women would not be married.

Commentary
This passage states the ruling that the slaughter of a Majusi (Magian) is impermissible, based on the hadith where the Prophet stipulated that for the Magians of Hajar who accepted jizyah, their slaughtered animals would not be eaten and their women would not be married. The commentary then extends this ruling by qiyas (analogy) to apostates (murtadd) and idol worshippers (wathani). The Hanafi school holds that the slaughter of a Majusi is not halal because they are not considered Ahl al-Kitab. The hadith is the primary proof. The hashiya explains the content of the letter.

Key Terms
مجوسي (Majūsī): A Zoroastrian fire-worshipper; considered not Ahl al-Kitab in Hanafi school.
مرتد (Murtadd): A Muslim who renounces Islam; his slaughter is invalid.
وثنى (Wathanī): Idol worshipper; one who worships idols.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The slaughter of a Majusi, apostate, and idol worshipper is haram because they are not Ahl al-Kitab, based on the Prophet's explicit condition in the hadith and qiyas.

Slaughter by Muhrim: Hanafi vs Shafi'i Dispute
Dispute on whether game slaughtered by a muhrim is permissible for others.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on game slaughtered by a muhrim, identify the proofs used by both Hanafis and Shafi'is, and explain the practical consequence of the dispute.

Core Idea
Game slaughtered by a muhrim is carrion for Hanafis; Shafi'is permit it for others because the muhrim's slaughter is valid.

When a person in ihram (muhrim) slaughters game, the schools differ sharply. The Hanafi school forbids it entirely, treating it as carrion, while Imam al-Shafi'i allows non-muhrims to eat it. This lesson examines the proofs each side presents and the practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed ruling
State the exact question: Is game slaughtered by a muhrim permissible for others to eat? The Hanafi says no, Shafi'i says yes.
The dispute hinges on whether the prohibition on hunting extends to slaughtering and consuming.
2
Examine the Hanafi proof
Read the Quranic verses (5:95-96) and the narration from Ata that the muhrim's game is not halal. Understand how the proof is derived.
The Hanafi rely on explicit prohibition of hunting in ihram and the athar of Ata.
3
Examine the Shafi'i counter-proof
Read the Shafi'i argument: the muhrim is a Muslim so his slaughter is valid; they cite the narration of al-Hakam ibn Utbah allowing consumption.
Shafi'is differentiate between the act of hunting (prohibited) and the act of slaughtering (valid).
4
Evaluate the tarjih
Consider which proof is stronger according to the Hanafi school. The Quranic verses and the athar of Ata are preferred over the athar of Hakam.
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi in the school.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical difference: if a muhrim slaughters game, Hanafis treat it as carrion; Shafi'is allow non-muhrims to eat it.
This affects real-life scenarios during Hajj/Umrah.

آیت میں ہے۔ حرم عليكم صيد البر ما دمتم حرما ( آیت ۹۶ سورۃ المائدة (۵) اور دوسری آیت میں ہے۔ یا ایها الذین آمنوا لا تقتلوا الصيد وانتم حرم (ب) ( آیت ۹۵ سورۃ المائدة (۵) ان دونوں آیتوں سے معلوم ہوا کہ محرم کو شکار نہیں کرنا چاہئے کیونکہ شکار کرنا اس پر حرام ہے۔ اور نہ شکار کرنے والوں کی مدد کرنی چاہئے۔ حضرت ابوقتادہ کی لمبی حدیث گزر چکی ہے کہ محرموں نے ان کی مدد نہیں کی۔ حدیث کا ٹکڑا یہ ہے ۔ عن عبد الله بن ابی قتادة . واستعنت بهم فابوا ان يعينوني (ج) ( بخاری شریف ، باب اذا اصاد الحلال فاهدى للحرم الصید اکلہ ص ۲۳۵ نمبر (۱۸۲) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ شکار کرنے والے کی محرم مدد بھی نہ کرے۔ اور محرم کا شکار کیا ہوا حلال نہیں ہے اس کی دلیل یہ اثر ہے۔ سألت الثورى عن المحرم يذبح صيدا هل يحل اكله لغيره ؟ فقال اخبرنى ليث عن عطاء انه قال لا يحل اكله لاحد (د) (مصنف عبد الرزاق ، باب الصيد وذبیحہ والتربص به ج رابع ص ۴۳۹ نمبر ۸۳۶۱) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ محرم کا ذبح کیا ہوا شکار کسی کے لئے حلال نہیں ہے۔
ہیں۔
امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ محرم کے لئے شکار کرنا اگر چہ حلال نہیں ہے لیکن اگر شکار کو ذبح کر دیا تو دوسروں کے لئے حلال ہے وہ کھا سکتے ہیں۔
محرم مسلمان ہے اس لئے اس کا ذبح کرنا جائز ہے (۲) اثر میں ہے۔ واخبرنی اشعث عن الحكم بن عتيبة انه قال لا بأس با کله (ه) (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب الصيد و ذبیحہ والتربص به ج رابع ص ۴۳۹ نمبر ۸۳۶۱) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ محرم کا ذبیحہ کھا سکتا ہے۔

حاشیہ : (ب) تم لوگوں پر خشکی کا شکار حرام کیا گیا ہے جب تک تم محرم ہو ۔ دوسری آیت میں ہے، اے ایمان والو! شکار کو قتل نہ کرو جب تم محرم ہو (ج) حضرت ابو قتادہ فرماتے ہیں۔ میں نے شکار کرنے کے لئے صحابہ سے مدد مانگی تو انہوں نے مدد کرنے سے انکار کیا۔ (و) حضرت ثورتی سے محرم کے بارے میں پوچھا کہ کیا وہ شکار ذبح کر سکتا ہے اور کیا دوسروں کے لئے اس کا ذبیحہ حلال ہے؟ فرمایا مجھ کو حضرت لیث نے حضرت عطاء سے خبر دی کہ اس کا کھانا کسی کے لئے حلال نہیں ہے (ہ) حضرت حکم بن عتیبہ نے فرمایا کہ محرم شکار ذبح کر دے تو دوسروں کے لئے کھانے میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے۔
And for the muhrim, catching game is not permissible, therefore slaughtering it is also not permissible. The verse says: 'Game of the land is made unlawful to you as long as you are in ihram' (Quran 5:96) and another verse: 'O you who believe, do not kill game while you are in ihram' (Quran 5:95). From these two verses it is known that a muhrim should not hunt, because hunting is forbidden for him. And he should not assist the hunters. The long hadith of Abu Qatadah has passed that the muhrims did not assist him. The portion of the hadith is: From Abdullah ibn Abi Qatadah: 'I sought their help but they refused to help me.' (Sahih al-Bukhari, Chapter: If a Halal Person Hunts and Gifts the Game to a Muhrim, he Eats it, p. 235, no. 182) From this hadith it is known that a muhrim should not even assist a hunter. And the game slaughtered by a muhrim is not halal. The proof for this is the following narration: 'I asked al-Thawri about a muhrim slaughtering game: Is it permissible for others to eat it? He said: Layth informed me from Ata that he said: It is not permissible for anyone to eat it.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, Chapter: Game and its Slaughter and Lying in Wait, vol. 4, p. 439, no. 8361) From this narration it is known that game slaughtered by a muhrim is not halal for anyone.

Imam Shafii says: Although hunting is not permissible for a muhrim, if he slaughters the game, it is halal for others and they can eat it. The muhrim is a Muslim, so his slaughter is permissible. And there is a narration: 'Ash'ath informed me from al-Hakam ibn Utbah that he said: There is no harm in eating it.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, same reference) From this narration it is known that the slaughter of a muhrim can be eaten.

Footnote (b): 'Game of the land is made unlawful to you as long as you are in ihram.' Another verse: 'O you who believe, do not kill game while you are in ihram.' (c) Abu Qatadah says: I sought the help of the Companions for hunting, but they refused to help. (d) [In OCR, (و)] Al-Thawri was asked about a muhrim slaughtering game: is it halal for others? He said: Layth informed me from Ata that its eating is not permissible for anyone. (e) Al-Hakam ibn Utbah said: If a muhrim slaughters game, there is no harm for others in eating it.
Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling and the Shafi'i dispute. The Hanafi school holds that a muhrim's slaughter of game is invalid and not permissible for anyone, based on Quranic prohibition of hunting in ihram and the narration of Ata from al-Thawri. The Shafi'i school, however, argues that since the muhrim is a Muslim, his slaughter is valid, and the prohibition is only on hunting, not on consuming the slaughtered meat. They cite the narration of al-Hakam ibn Utbah. The commentary does not provide a clear Hanafi response, but the weight of the text suggests the Hanafi position remains the relied-upon view. The hashiya explains the proofs.

Key Terms
محرم (Muḥrim): A person in the state of ihram (during Hajj or Umrah) for whom hunting is prohibited.
صید (Ṣayd): Game; wild animals that are permissible to hunt when not in ihram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a person in ihram (muhrim) slaughters game, what is the ruling for others to eat it?
A) Halal for everyone
B) Halal only if the muhrim was forgetful
C) Not halal for anyone
D) Halal only for the muhrim himself

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school strictly prohibits eating game slaughtered by a muhrim, treating it as carrion, based on Quranic verses and the narration of Ata.

Tasmiyah Omission: Intentional vs Forgetful Slaughter
Ruling on consuming meat when tasmiyah is omitted intentionally or forgetfully, with school disputes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on consuming meat when tasmiyah is omitted intentionally vs forgetfully, compare it with the Shafi'i and Maliki positions, and identify the key proofs.

Core Idea
Intentional omission of tasmiyah invalidates slaughter; forgetfulness does not — intention changes the ruling.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position on tasmiyah during slaughter. The central issue is whether the omission of saying Bismillah — whether intentional or forgetful — renders the meat impermissible. The Hanafi school distinguishes between the two, while the Shafi'i and Maliki schools take different stances. We will explore the textual proofs and the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what tasmiyah is and its legal status (wajib in Hanafi school). Understand that the passage concerns the effect of omitting it.
Tasmiyah is saying 'Bismillah' at the time of slaughter.
2
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi ruling: intentional omission makes the animal carrion (haram); forgetful omission makes it halal. Note the distinction based on intention.
3
Examine the Hanafi proofs
Identify the Quranic verse (6:121) and the hadith (Adi ibn Hatim, Ibn Abbas) that support the Hanafi position. Notice how the verse is general but the hadith provides an exception for forgetfulness.
The hadith of Ibn Abbas explicitly allows eating if the slaughterer forgets and later says Bismillah.
4
Compare with opposing schools
Learn the Shafi'i position (both intentional and forgetful are halal) and the Maliki position (both are haram). Understand their proofs: the Shafi'i rely on the hadith that 'a Muslim suffices by his name'; the Maliki take the Quranic verse as absolute.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Recognize the practical difference: in the Hanafi school, a forgetful slaughterer's meat is halal, but if intentional, it is haram. In Shafi'i, both are halal. In Maliki, both are haram. This affects daily practice.

Source Text

حاشیہ : (الف) جب تک جانور پر بسم اللہ نہ پڑھا گیا ہو مت کھاؤ اس لئے کہ وہ فسق ہے (ب) حضرت عدی بن حاتم سے کہتے ہوئے سنا... آپ نے فرمایامت کھاؤ اس لئے کہ اپنے کتے پر بسم اللہ پڑھے ہو دوسروں کے کتے پر بسم اللہ نہیں پڑھے ہو ( ج) آپ نے فرمایا مسلمان کو اللہ کا نام کافی ہے پس اگر ذبح کرتے وقت بھول گیا تو بسم اللہ پڑھ کر کھالے جائز ہے (1) حضرت ابن عباس نے فرمایا جو ذبح کرتے وقت بسم اللہ بھول جائے تو کوئی حرج کی بات نہیں ہے (ہ) حضرت عائشہ نے حضور سے پوچھا کہ کچھ قوم میرے پاس گوشت لے کر آتے ہیں، مجھے معلوم نہیں کہ اس پر بسم اللہ پڑھا ہے یا نہیں؟ آپ نے فرمایا اس پر بسم اللہ پڑھو اور کھا لو۔ (و) حضرت ابن عباس نے فرمایا اگر مسلمان نے ذبح کیا اور بسم اللہ نہیں پڑھا تو کھائے اس لئے کہ مسلمان کے دل میں اللہ کا نام ہے۔
2603 (24) And if the slaughterer leaves off the tasmiyah intentionally, then the slaughtered animal is carrion, not to be eaten; and if he leaves it off forgetfully, it is eaten. (24) If the slaughterer intentionally leaves off Bismillah, the slaughtered animal is like carrion and is not eaten; if he leaves it off forgetfully, it will be eaten. In the verse: 'And do not eat of that upon which the name of Allah has not been mentioned, for indeed it is grave disobedience.' (Quran 6:121) (a) (2) In connection with hunting, this hadith has passed: 'I heard Adi ibn Hatim... He said: Do not eat, for you have mentioned the name of Allah over your dog, and not over the other.' (Sahih al-Bukhari, Chapter: Hunting with the Mi'rad, p. 823, no. 5476) From this hadith it is known that if Bismillah is recited, eat; if not, do not eat.

And if Bismillah is left out forgetfully, then eat; the proof is this hadith: From Ibn Abbas that the Prophet said: 'The Muslim suffices by his name. So if he forgets to recite (the name) while slaughtering, then let him recite and mention the name of Allah, then eat.' (al-Daraqutni, Book of Drinks, vol. 4, p. 198, no. 4762) A similar meaning is found in Bukhari as the saying of Abdullah ibn Abbas: 'Whoever forgets, there is no harm.' (Sahih al-Bukhari, Chapter: Tasmiyah over the Slaughtered Animal, p. 826, no. 5498; Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Chapter: Whoever Leaves Tasmiyah and His Slaughter is Permissible, vol. 9, p. 401, no. 18890) From this hadith it is known that if Bismillah is left out forgetfully, it is halal and can be eaten. (2) The hadith of Aisha: 'Some people said to the Prophet: Some people bring us meat and we do not know whether the name of Allah has been mentioned over it or not? He said: Recite Bismillah over it yourselves and eat it.' (Sahih al-Bukhari, Chapter: The Slaughter of Bedouins and Their Like, p. 828, no. 5507) From this hadith it is also known that if it is not known whether Bismillah was recited or not, it is halal. Imam al-Shafi'i says: Whether left out forgetfully or intentionally, as long as the slaughterer is Muslim or from the People of the Book, it is eaten in both cases. Their proof is this hadith: From Ibn Abbas: 'If a Muslim slaughters and does not mention the name of Allah, let him eat, for in the Muslim is a name from the names of Allah.' (al-Daraqutni, Book of Drinks, vol. 4, p. 198, no. 4760; Sunan al-Bayhaqi, same chapter, vol. 9, p. 401, no. 18891) From this hadith it is known that even if a Muslim intentionally leaves off Bismillah, the slaughtered animal is halal because Allah's name is in his heart. Imam Malik says: Even if left out forgetfully, the slaughtered animal is not halal. He says the verse 'Do not eat of that upon which the name of Allah has not been mentioned' is general, that in no circumstance should it be eaten without Bismillah, whether left out forgetfully or intentionally.

Footnotes: (a) Do not eat until Bismillah has been recited over the animal, because that is a sin. (b) I heard Adi ibn Hatim... He said: Do not eat, because you have recited over your dog and not over the other. (c) He said: The Muslim suffices by his name. So if he forgets to recite (the name) while slaughtering, let him recite Bismillah and eat, permissible. (d) Ibn Abbas said: Whoever forgets to recite (at slaughter), there is no harm. (e) Aisha asked the Prophet: Some people bring meat, I do not know if Bismillah was recited on it? He said: Recite Bismillah over it and eat. (f) Ibn Abbas said: If a Muslim slaughters and does not recite Bismillah, let him eat, because in the Muslim is a name from the names of Allah.
Source pages p. 27

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling on tasmiyah: intentional omission invalidates the slaughter (makes it carrion), but forgetfulness does not. This is based on the Quranic verse (6:121) and the hadith about hunting with dogs. The Shafi'i school permits eating in both cases, citing a hadith that a Muslim inherently bears Allah's name. The Maliki school prohibits both, taking the verse as general. The Hanafi position distinguishes between intentional and forgetful, as supported by the hadith of Ibn Abbas and the practice of the Companions. The hashiya explains the proofs.

Key Terms
تسمية (Tasmiyah): The act of saying 'Bismillah' (in the name of Allah) before slaughtering an animal.
ذبيحة (Dhābīḥah): The slaughtered animal; its meat is halal if conditions are met.
عمدا (Amdan): Intentionally, with full knowledge and choice.
ناسيا (Nāsiyan): Forgetfully, without intention to omit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a Muslim slaughterer forgets to say Bismillah while slaughtering, what is the ruling on the meat?
A) It is halal
B) It is haram
C) It is makruh
D) It is permissible only if he remembers later

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the omission of tasmiyah invalidates slaughter only if intentional; forgetfulness is excused, making the meat halal.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Minimum Veins for Dhabh
Intra-Hanafi dispute on minimum veins for dhabh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the minimum veins to cut for valid dhabh and apply the hadith evidence to each position.

Core Idea
Valid slaughter requires cutting most veins; Sahibayn insist on three specific ones to ensure full blood flow.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute on the minimum requirements for valid slaughter (dhabh). While all agree that cutting the veins (awdaj) is essential, Imam Abu Hanifa holds that cutting the majority suffices, whereas his two principal students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), require cutting the halqum (throat), mari' (gullet), and one of the two jugular veins. We will analyze the textual evidence each side uses and understand the practical consequence of this difference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Required Veins
The text mentions four veins: al-halqum (throat/trachea), al-mari' (gullet/esophagus), and al-wadajan (the two jugular veins). Understand their locations and functions.
These are the 'awdaj' referred to in the hadith.
2
State Abu Hanifa's Position
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that cutting the majority (akthar) of these four veins suffices. In practice, cutting at least three of them is valid.
He considers the plural 'awdaj' in the hadith as indicating any of the veins.
3
State the Sahibayn's Position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani require cutting three specific veins: al-halqum, al-mari', and one of the two jugulars. They argue this ensures complete blood drainage.
This is the more precautionary view.
4
Examine the Evidence
Both sides use the hadith: 'Everything that cuts the awdaj' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah) and the practice of Ibn Umar. Abu Hanifa interprets 'awdaj' as a general plural; the Sahibayn view it as referring to the specific veins mentioned in other traditions. Cutting to the bone (as per Ibn Umar) ensures all necessary veins are cut.
The practical difference (thamarah): If only two veins are cut, the dhabh is valid according to Abu Hanifa but invalid according to the Sahibayn.

Source Text

الشرح الثميرى الجزء الرابع ۲۲ كتاب الصيد اكثرها فكذلك عند ابي حنيفة رحمه الله وقالا لا بد من قطع الحلقوم والمرئ واحد الودجين اكثر كل کے حکم میں ہے اس لئے تین چار میں سے اکثر ہے اس لئے اتنا کافی ہے۔ فائده صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ حلقوم بھی کاٹنا ہو گا اور مری بھی اور دوشہ رگوں میں سے ایک کو کاٹنا ہوگا تا کہ شہ رگ سے پورا خون نکل جائے۔ اور ہر ایک رگ کا ایک ایک ضرور ہو جائے۔ حدیث میں ہے کہ ور جان کالے اس لئے ور جان یعنی شہ رگ میں سے ایک کا نا ضروری ہے۔ عن رافع بن خديج قال سالت رسول الله الله عن الذبيحة بالليط فقال كل ما افرى الاوداج الا سن او ظفر (الف) ( مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ۳۲ من قال اذا انصر الدم فكل ما خلا سنا او عظماج رابع ص ۲۵۹ نمبر ۱۹۸۰۳) حضرت ابن عمر کا قول ہے۔ ان ابن عمر نهى عن النخع يقول يقطع مادون العظم ثم يدع حتى يموت (ب) ( بخاری شریف ، باب الخمر والذبح ص ۸۲۸ نمبر ۵۵۱۰) اس حدیث واثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ ہڈی تک کاٹ دے اور چھوڑ دے۔ اور ہڈی تک کاٹے گا تو مری ، حلقوم اور شہ رگ کٹ جائیں گے۔ اور اوراج کا کاٹنا اس لئے ضروری ہے کہ حدیث میں اور اج کاٹنے کی تاکید ہر موقع پر ہے۔
The commentary on Samari, volume 4, page 22, Book of Hunting. 'Most of it, thus according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him. And they said: It is necessary to cut the throat (halqum), the gullet (mari'), and one of the two jugular veins (wadajayn).' Urdu: 'In the ruling of the majority it is the same, so among three or four (veins) what is majority is sufficient. Benefit: Sahibayn say that the throat (halqum) must also be cut, and the gullet (mari') also, and one of the two jugular veins (shah rag) so that full blood comes out from the jugular. And every vein's one cut is necessary.' 'In hadith it is said that the jugular vein is called, so one of the jugular veins is necessary. From Rafi' ibn Khadij who said: I asked the Messenger of Allah about the slaughter using a reed, and he said: Everything that cuts the veins, except a tooth or a nail (reference to Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah). And the statement of Ibn Umar: He forbade nakh' (cutting the spinal cord), saying: Cut below the bone then leave until it dies (Reference to Sahih Bukhari).' From this hadith and athar it became clear that one should cut to the bone and leave. And when one cuts to the bone, the gullet, throat, and jugular veins are cut. And cutting the awdaj (veins) is necessary because the hadith emphasizes cutting the awdaj on every occasion.
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage opens the Book of Hunting (Kitab al-Sayd) by addressing the minimum requirement for valid slaughter (dhabh). It begins with an intra-Hanafi dispute: according to Abu Hanifa, cutting the majority of the required veins is sufficient. The required veins are generally considered four: the throat (halqum), the gullet (mari'), and the two jugular veins (wadajan). Abu Hanifa's position is that if most of these are cut (i.e., at least three), the slaughter is valid. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that one must cut the halqum, mari', and at least one of the two jugular veins. The commentary then provides textual evidence: a hadith from Rafi' ibn Khadij where the Prophet defines permissible slaughter as anything that cuts the veins (awdaj), except tooth or nail. This hadith is used by both positions. The second evidence is the practice of Ibn Umar, who forbade cutting the spinal cord (nakh') and instructed to cut below the bone and then let the animal die. The commentator explains that cutting to the bone ensures that the required veins are cut. The overall argument is that cutting the awdaj is necessary based on these sources.

Key Terms
الحلقوم (al-halqum): The throat; specifically the windpipe (trachea) that carries air to the lungs.
المرئ (al-mari'): The gullet; the esophagus that carries food.
الودجان (al-wadajan): The two jugular veins on either side of the neck.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn, which combination of veins must be cut for valid dhabh?
A) Most of the four veins (majority)
B) Halqum, mari', and one wadaj
C) Only the two jugular veins
D) All four veins

Key Takeaway
For valid dhabh, the Sahibayn require cutting halqum, mari’, and one wadaj; the mufta bihi follows this stricter view.

Permissible Instruments for Slaughter
Ruling on valid tools for dhabh based on hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on permissible slaughter instruments, identify the exception of attached tooth and nail, and explain the rationale based on the hadith.

Core Idea
Any sharp object that makes blood flow is valid for slaughter, except an attached tooth or nail.

This lesson addresses a common question: what tools can be used for dhabh (Islamic slaughter)? The Hanafi school rules based on the hadith of Rafi' ibn Khadij, focusing on the effect (making blood flow) rather than the material. We will examine the general permission, the exception of attached tooth and nail, and the reasoning that even unusual materials like a sharp reed or stone are valid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its exception
State the general Hanafi position: slaughter is permissible with any sharp instrument that makes blood flow, with the exception of an attached tooth (sinn) and an attached nail (zifr).
The exception applies only when they are attached; if detached and sharp, they become permissible.
2
Locate the dalil (evidence)
Find the hadith of Rafi' ibn Khadij in the source text. Note that it is from Sunan Abi Dawud, Sahih al-Bukhari, and Sunan al-Nasa'i.
The hadith is ahad (single-narrator), so its thubut is zanni (probable).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (indication)
The Prophet's command 'make blood flow' (anhar al-dam) establishes the criterion: any tool that cuts and lets blood out is valid. The exception of tooth (bone) and nail (used by Abyssinians) is explained because they are attached and cause strangulation.
The Hanafi rely on the general permission and restrict the exception to attached condition.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani has a transmission that even detached tooth and nail are prohibited. The preferred view (mufta bihi) is that they are permissible if detached and sharp.
The text's commentary explicitly favours the detached-and-sharp view.
5
Apply the ruling to examples
The passage explicitly allows a reed (laytah) and sharp stone (marwah). Confirm that any sharp object fulfilling the condition is valid.
This covers modern scenarios like a sharp piece of glass or metal, as long as it is not an attached tooth/nail.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويجوز الذبح بالليطة والمروة وبكل شيء انهر الدم الا السن القائم والظفر القائم بانس کا ٹکڑا جو پتلا اور دھاردار ہو یا تیز پتھر ہو یا ہر وہ چیز جو دھاردار ہو جس سے رگیں کٹ کر خون بہنے لگے۔ البتہ تالو میں لگے دانت اور انگلی میں لگے ہوئے ناخن سے ذبح کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ بانس کے ٹکڑے اور دھار دار پتھر سے ذبح کرنا جائز ہے اس لئے کہ حدیث میں ہے۔ عن رافع بن خديج قال اتيت رسول الله لله فقلت يا رسول الله ! انا نلقى العدو غدا وليس معنا مدى افنذبح بالمروة وشقة العصا ؟ فقال رسول الله الله ارن او اعجل ما انهر الدم وذكر اسم الله عليه فكلوا مالم يكن سن وظفر وساحدثكم عن ذلك اما السن فعظم واما الظفر فمدى الحبشة (ج) ( ابو داؤد شریف، باب الذبيحه بالمروة ص۳۳ نمبر ۲۸۲ / بخاری شریف، باب ما انهر الدم من القصب والمروة والحدید ص ۸۲۷ نمبر ۵۵۰۳ ، نسائی شریف، اباحة الذبح بالقووص ۶۱۱ نمبر ۴۴۰۶) اس حدیث سے یہ بھی معلوم ہوا کہ کوئی بھی دھار دار چیز جو خون جاری کر دے اس سے ذبح کرنا جائز ہے۔ اور یہ بھی معلوم ہوا کہ بانس کی بتی اور دھار دار پتھر سے ذبح کرنا جائز ہے۔ اور یہ بھی معلوم ہوا کہ لگا ہوا دانت اور لگا ہوا ناخن سے ذبح کرنا جائز نہیں ہے کیونکہ لگے ہوئے ہونے کی وجہ سے متفقہ یعنی گلا دبا کر مارنے کی شکل ہو جائے گی۔ کیونکہ لگے ہوئے ہونے کی وجہ سے دانت سے دبائے گا اور ناخن سے بھی دبائے گا جس کی وجہ سے موت واقع ہوگی۔ اس لئے جائز نہیں ہے۔ لیکن اگر ناخن اور دانت جسم سے الگ ہو چکے ہوں اور دھاردار ہوں تو ان سے حلال ہو جائے گا۔ اس صورت میں حدیث میں اسن اور ظفر سے مراد السن القائم اور الظفر القائم ہوگا اور حدیث کا انداز بھی یہی بتا رہا ہے۔
It is permissible to slaughter with a reed (laytah), a sharp stone (marwah), and every thing that makes blood flow except an attached tooth and an attached nail. Urdu: 'A piece of bamboo that is thin and sharp, or a sharp stone, or every sharp thing that cuts veins and makes blood flow. However, it is not permissible to slaughter with a tooth attached to the palate or a nail attached to the finger. Slaughter with a piece of bamboo and sharp stone is permissible because the hadith says: From Rafi' ibn Khadij who said: I came to the Messenger of Allah and said: O Messenger of Allah, we will meet the enemy tomorrow and we do not have knives with us. Can we slaughter with sharp stones and the split part of a stick? He said: Hasten to make blood flow and mention the name of Allah over it, so eat, except what is cut with a tooth and a nail. I will tell you about that: As for the tooth, it is a bone; as for the nail, it is the knife of the Abyssinians.' (references to Sunan Abi Dawud, Sahih al-Bukhari, Sunan al-Nasa'i) From this hadith it was also learned that any sharp thing that makes blood flow, slaughtering with it is permissible. And it was also learned that slaughtering with an attached tooth and an attached nail is not permissible because due to being attached, it becomes similar to strangling; because with attached ones, he will press with the tooth and press with the nail, causing death. Therefore it is not permissible. But if the nail and tooth have become detached from the body and are sharp, then it becomes permissible. In that case, in the hadith, 'sinn' and 'zifr' mean the attached tooth and the attached nail, and the style of the hadith indicates this.'
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage states the general rule for valid slaughtering tools: any sharp object that makes blood flow is permissible. The examples given are a reed (laytah) and a sharp stone (marwah). The exception is an attached tooth and an attached nail. The commentary explains the reason: attached tooth and nail press the throat and cause death by constriction, not by clean cutting, which is akin to strangulation and thus invalid. However, if the tooth or nail is detached and sharp, it becomes a permissible tool because it cuts cleanly. The hadith of Rafi' ibn Khadij is cited as proof: the Prophet permitted all instruments that make blood flow except tooth and nail. The Prophet explained that tooth is a bone (which is not sharp) and nail is used by Abyssinians (for cutting, but when attached it is not suitable for hygienic slaughter). The commentary clarifies that the attached status is the key factor.

Key Terms
الليطة (al-laytah): A reed or thin stick with a sharp edge; used as a cutting tool.
المروة (al-marwah): A sharp stone; any flint or sharp-edged rock.
انهر الدم (anhar al-dam): Made blood flow; the key condition for a valid slaughter instrument is that it causes blood to flow out.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith cited, why is slaughter with an attached tooth invalid?
A) Because the tooth is a bone.
B) Because it is not made of iron.
C) Because it causes death by strangulation rather than cutting.
D) Because it is not sharp.

Key Takeaway
The primary criterion for a valid slaughter tool is that it is sharp and causes blood to flow; the only categorical exceptions are an attached tooth and an attached nail due to the risk of strangulation.

The Recommendation to Sharpen the Knife for Slaughter
Ruling on sharpening knife as a recommended act for dhabh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on sharpening the knife before dhabh and explain its proof from the hadith.

Core Idea
Sharpening the knife before slaughter is a confirmed sunnah, not obligatory, because the command is in the context of ihsan.

This lesson addresses a practical sunnah in the act of slaughter: ensuring the knife is sharp before cutting. The Hanafi school considers this a mustahabb (recommended) act, based on a prophetic hadith that commands excellence in all things, including slaughter. Understanding this ruling helps distinguish between what is required and what is recommended.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is sharpening the knife before dhabh. The ruling is mustahabb (sunnah muakkadah).
The text explicitly says 'yustahabb'.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith of Shaddad ibn Aws recorded in Sahih Muslim and Sunan Abi Dawud.
The dalil is a hadith ahad.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The command 'let one of you sharpen his knife' indicates recommendation because it is embedded in the command to do ihsan, which is recommended, not obligatory.
The word 'ihsan' signals excellence, not obligation.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
There is no significant ikhtilaf; all schools agree it is recommended.
Cross-madhhab status: muttafaq alayh.
5
Determine the thamarah
Practical consequence: if one does not sharpen, the slaughter is still valid but it is makruh tanzihi to cause extra pain.
The act is not a condition of validity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويستحب ان يحدَّ الذابح شفرته تا کہ جانور کو بلا وجہ تکلیف نہ ہو حدیث میں اس کی تاکید ہے۔ عن شداد بن اوس قال ثنتان حفظتهما عن رسول الله ل الله قال ان الله كتب الاحسان على كل شيء فاذا قتلتم فاحسنوا القتلة واذا ذبحتم فاحسنوا الذبح وليحد احدكم شفرته فليرح ذبيحته (الف) ( مسلم شریف، باب الامر باحسان الذبح والقتل وتحديد الشفر پاص ۱۵۲ نمبر ۱۹۵۵ را بو داؤد شریف ، باب فی انھی ان تصير البهائم والرفق بالذيجي ص ۳۳ نمبر ۲۸۱۴) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ چھری اچھی طرح تیز کرنا مستحب ہے۔ محد: تیز کرنا۔ شفرة : لمبی چھری۔
It is recommended (mustahabb) for the slaughterer to sharpen his knife. So that the animal is not unnecessarily harmed. The hadith emphasizes this. From Shaddad ibn Aws who said: I memorized two things from the Messenger of Allah: 'Indeed Allah has prescribed excellence (ihsan) in everything. So when you kill, kill well; and when you slaughter, slaughter well. Let one of you sharpen his knife and give relief to his animal.' (Reference to Sahih Muslim and Sunan Abi Dawud). From this hadith it became clear that sharpening the knife well is mustahabb. 'Midd': sharpening. 'Shifrah': long knife.
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage states a recommended (mustahabb) act for the person performing slaughter: to sharpen the knife before slaughtering. The proof is a well-known hadith narrated by Shaddad ibn Aws in which the Prophet commands excellence (ihsan) in all actions, specifically in slaughter: sharpen the knife and give comfort to the animal by making the cut swift and clean. The commentary explains that this is to prevent unnecessary suffering of the animal. The hadith is from Sahih Muslim and Sunan Abi Dawud. The passage is straightforward: sharpening the knife is not obligatory but is highly recommended.

Key Terms
شفرة (shafrah): A knife or blade used for slaughter; specifically a long knife.
الاحسان (al-ihsan): Excellence; doing something in the best possible way. In slaughter, it includes sharpening the knife and slaughtering swiftly.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on sharpening the knife before dhabh according to this passage?
A) It is obligatory (fard).
B) It is recommended (mustahabb).
C) It is required (wajib).
D) It is neutral (mubah).

Key Takeaway
Sharpening the knife before dhabh is a confirmed sunnah rooted in the hadith of ihsan; omitting it does not invalidate the slaughter but loses the reward.

Ruling on Cutting the Spinal Cord or Severing the Head During Slaughter
Ruling with proof: nakh' (cutting spinal cord) is makruh, meat halal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on nakh' (cutting the spinal cord) and explain why the meat remains halal despite the disliked action.

Core Idea
Cutting the spinal cord is makruh, but the meat is halal if the essential veins are severed.

A butcher may unintentionally or carelessly cut beyond the bone into the spinal cord, or even sever the head completely. What is the legal status of the slaughtered animal? This lesson clarifies that such an act is disliked (makruh) but does not render the meat unlawful, provided the required veins are cut. The proof lies in the practice of Ibn Umar (may Allah be pleased with him), who forbade nakh' but did not declare the meat haram.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act in question
Determine what 'nakh'' refers to: cutting the spinal cord (haram mukh) or severing the head during slaughter.
Distinguish this from the required cuts (halqum, mari', wadaj).
2
State the Hanafi ruling
The ruling is makruh tanzihi (lightly disliked). The meat is halal because the four essential veins have been cut.
The ruling applies whether the action is intentional or accidental.
3
Identify the proof (dalil)
The proof is the athar from Ibn Umar: he forbade nakh' and instructed to cut below the bone and then let the animal die. This indicates that cutting beyond the bone is disliked, not invalidating.
The hadith is from Sahih Bukhari, transmitted via Nafi'.
4
Derive the rationale (wajh al-dalalah)
Ibn Umar's prohibition shows that nakh' is discouraged, but his instruction to 'cut below the bone' implies that the essential cut is below the bone. Cutting above does not nullify slaughter.
The word 'nahā' (forbade) indicates karahah, not tahrim, because the meat remains halal.
5
Apply the ruling to practice
If a butcher cuts the spinal cord or severs the head, the meat is lawful. However, it is makruh to do so intentionally.
The act is sinful only in the sense of being disliked; the slaughter is valid.

Source Text

كسی نے چھری حرام مغز تک پہنچادی یا سرکاٹ دی تو اس کے لئے یہ مکروہ ہے اور اس کا ذبیحہ کھایا جائے گا۔ گلے میں جو ہڈی ہوتی ہے اس کے درمیان میں موٹی رگیں ہوتی ہیں جن کو حرام مغز کہتے ہیں۔ ذبح میں ہڈی تک چھری پہنچانا چاہئے اس سے ذبح مکمل ہو جاتا ہے اس سے زیادہ تکلیف نہیں دینی چاہئے لیکن کسی نے ہڈی کے اندر تک یعنی حرام مغز تک چھری چھودی یا پوری گردن کاٹ دی تو ایسا کرنا مکروہ ہے۔ البتہ ایسا کرنے سے حلقوم ، مری اور ود جان سب کٹ گئے اس لئے ذبیحہ حلال ہو گیا۔ اخبرنی نافع ان ابن عمر نهى عن النخع يقول يقطع مادون العظم ثم يدع حتى يموت (ب) ( بخاری شریف، باب حاشیہ : (الف) حضور سے منقول ہے کہ اللہ نے ہر چیز پر احسان فرض کیا ہے۔ پس جب قتل کرو تو اچھی طرح قتل کرو اور ذبح کرو تو اچھی طرح ذبح کرو اور اپنی چھری تیز کر لو اور ذبیحہ کو ٹھنڈا ہونے دو (ب) حضرت ابن عمر ر و کتے تھے تجھے یعنی حرام مغز تک چھری لے جانے سے، فرماتے تھے ہڈی سے پہلے پہلے تک کاٹ دے پھر چھوڑ دے یہاں تک کہ مرجائے۔
If someone makes the knife reach the 'haram mukh' (spinal cord) or cuts off the head, then it is makruh for him and his slaughtered animal will be eaten. In the neck, there is a bone, and inside it are thick veins called 'haram mukh'. In slaughter, the knife should reach the bone; this completes the slaughter. One should not cause more pain beyond that. But if someone pierces inside the bone, i.e., up to the 'haram mukh', or cuts the whole neck, then doing so is makruh. Nevertheless, by doing so, the throat, gullet, and jugular veins are all cut, so the slaughtering is halal. Nafi' informed me that Ibn Umar forbade nakh' (cutting the spinal cord), saying: 'Cut below the bone and then leave until it dies.' (Reference to Sahih Bukhari, chapter...).
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage rules on an act sometimes done during slaughter: cutting through the bone into the spinal cord (nakh') or completely severing the head. Such action is makruh (disliked) because it causes unnecessary suffering and violates the recommended practice of cutting only the required veins. However, the meat remains halal because the essential veins (halqum, mari', and wadaj) have been cut. The proof is the practice of Ibn Umar, who forbade nakh' (cutting the spinal cord) and instructed to cut below the bone and then let the animal die. This indicates that cutting beyond the bone is not prohibited to the point of invalidating the dhabh, but it is discouraged.

Key Terms
النخع (al-nakh'): Cutting the spinal cord or severing the vertebrae; a prohibited practice in slaughter.
حرام مغز (haram mukh): Literal 'forbidden marrow'; refers to the spinal cord within the vertebrae.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The meat is haraam.
B) The meat is halal but the act is makruh.
C) The slaughter is invalid and must be repeated.
D) The act is ideal and recommended.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, cutting the spinal cord or head during slaughter is disliked (makruh) but does not make the meat haram, provided the four essential veins are cut.

Valid Slaughter Tools: The Tooth and Nail Exception
Explains valid slaughter tools and the exception for attached tooth and nail

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that any tool causing blood flow is valid for slaughter, and distinguish between prohibited attached tooth/nail and permissible detached sharp alternatives.

Core Idea
A tool is valid if it causes blood flow; an attached tooth or nail kills by pressure, not slaughter.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on acceptable slaughter tools. The general principle is that any instrument that makes blood flow (inhar al-dam) is permissible. However, a specific exception exists for the tooth and nail when they are attached to a living body, because they cause death by strangulation rather than proper slaughter. We will explore the hadith evidence, the reasoning behind the distinction, and an intra-Hanafi disagreement on whether detached tooth/nail are also prohibited.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule
State the Hanafi principle: any tool that causes blood to flow (inhar al-dam) is valid for slaughter. This includes bamboo strips and sharp stones.
The rule is based on the hadith 'kullu ma anhara al-dam' (anything that causes blood to flow).
2
Identify the exception
Recognize that an attached tooth (al-sinn al-qa'im) and attached nail (al-zufr al-qa'im) are invalid because they kill by pressure, not by cutting and blood flow.
The Prophet prohibited using a tooth or nail for slaughter.
3
Understand the reasoning
The attached tooth/nail cause death by pressing and strangling, which does not fulfill the requirement of causing blood flow (inhar al-dam).
This is why they are considered haram tools.
4
Apply the distinction
Note that if the tooth or nail is detached from the body and sharp, it becomes like any other sharp tool and is permissible, because it can now cause blood flow by cutting.
The hadith prohibition is interpreted to refer only to attached ones (al-qa'im).
5
Consider the intra-Hanafi disagreement
Imam Muhammad narrates that the hadith prohibits tooth and nail absolutely, including detached ones, but the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that detached sharp ones are permissible.
The text prefers the first interpretation based on the style of the hadith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن خون جاری کر دے اس سے ذبح کرنا جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ کل ما انهر الدم سے کوئی بھی چیز جو خون جاری کر دے مراد ہے۔ اور یہ بھی معلوم ہوا کہ بانس کی بتی اور دھار دار پتھر سے ذبح کرنا جائز ہے۔ اور یہ بھی معلوم ہوا کہ لگا ہوا دانت اور لگا ہوا ناخن سے ذبح کرنا جائز نہیں ہے کیونکہ لگے ہوئے ہونے کی وجہ سے متفقہ یعنی گلا دبا کر مارنے کی شکل ہو جائے گی۔ کیونکہ لگے ہوئے ہونے کی وجہ سے دانت سے دبائے گا اور ناخن سے بھی دبائے گا جس کی وجہ سے موت واقع ہوگی۔ اس لئے جائز نہیں ہے۔ لیکن اگر ناخن اور دانت جسم سے الگ ہو چکے ہوں اور دھاردار ہوں تو ان سے حلال ہو جائے گا۔ اس صورت میں حدیث میں اسن اور ظفر سے مراد السن القائم اور الظفر القائم ہوگا اور حدیث کا انداز بھی یہی بتا رہا ہے۔ فائده امام محمد کی ایک روایت ہے کہ اوپر کی حدیث میں مطلقا دانت اور ناخن سے ذبح کرنے کو منع فرمایا ہے اس لئے الگ شدہ ناخن اور دانت سے بھی ذبیحہ نہ کرے۔ انت لطہ : بانس کی بتی ، بانس کا دھاردار چھلکا۔ المروة : دھار دار پتھر ۔ انھر : خون بہا دے۔ السن القائم : لگا ہوادانت۔ الظفر ناخن
And whoever makes blood flow with it, slaughtering with it is permissible. Because 'everything that causes blood to flow' is intended. And it is also known that slaughtering with a bamboo strip and a sharp stone is permissible. And it is also known that slaughtering with an attached tooth and an attached nail is not permissible, because being attached results in strangulation, i.e., it becomes a form of squeezing to death. Because being attached, the tooth will press and the nail will also press, causing death. Therefore it is not permissible. But if the nail and tooth have become separated from the body and are sharp, then it becomes halal. In that case, the meaning of 'tooth' and 'nail' in the hadith is the attached tooth and the attached nail, and the style of the hadith also indicates this. Benefit: There is a narration from Imam Muhammad that the above hadith absolutely prohibits slaughtering with tooth and nail, so one should not slaughter with a detached nail and tooth either. 'Lat' means bamboo strip, the sharp peel of bamboo. 'Marwah' means sharp stone. 'Anhar' means to cause blood to flow. 'Al-sinn al-qa'im' means attached tooth. 'Al-zufr' means nail.
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage discusses the valid tools for slaughter in Hanafi fiqh. The general principle is that any instrument that causes blood to flow (inhar al-dam) is permissible for slaughter. This includes bamboo strips and sharp stones. However, the tooth and nail of a living animal are not permissible because they are attached and cause death by strangulation rather than proper slaughter. If the tooth or nail is detached and sharp, it is permissible. The hadith prohibiting 'tooth and nail' is interpreted to refer to attached ones only. Imam Muhammad has a narration that prohibits even detached ones, but the relied-upon position is that detached and sharp ones are permissible. The passage also provides definitions of key terms.

Key Terms
السن القائم (al-sinn al-qa'im): An attached tooth (part of a living body)
الظفر القائم (al-zufr al-qa'im): An attached nail (part of a living body)
انھر الدم (inhar al-dam): Causing blood to flow (the condition for valid slaughter)

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Attached tooth
B) Sharp bamboo strip
C) Detached nail but not sharp
D) Attached nail

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits slaughter with any tool that causes blood flow, except an attached tooth or nail because they kill by pressure.

Ruling on Cutting the Spinal Cord or Severing the Head
Ruling that cutting the spinal cord or head is makruh but the meat is halal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on cutting the spinal cord or head during slaughter, explain why it is makruh but the meat is halal, and identify the key evidence (dalil) from hadith and athar.

Core Idea
Cutting the spinal cord or head is makruh but does not invalidate slaughter – the meat remains halal.

In fiqh al-dhabh (slaughter), precision and kindness are emphasized. This lesson addresses a common concern: what if the spinal cord (nakh') is cut or the head is severed during slaughter? The Hanafi school clarifies that while such actions are discouraged (makruh) due to unnecessary pain, they do not render the meat unlawful. We will examine the ruling, its rationale, and the supporting evidence from the Companions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
State the act: cutting the spinal cord (nakh') or the head during slaughter. Identify the hukm: makruh tanzihi (disliked, not sinful). Recognize that the meat is still halal.
The act is not haram, only disliked.
2
Understand why it is makruh
The reason is that it causes unnecessary pain or may cause the animal to die before complete bleeding. The text states one should not cause more pain than needed.
Kindness to animals is a principle.
3
Recognize why the meat remains halal
The essential parts (halqum, mari', and wadajain) are still cut, allowing proper bleeding. The presence of these cuts ensures the slaughter is valid.
The act of slaughter (dhabh) is defined by cutting these vessels.
4
Examine the evidence: hadith and athar
Read the hadith of Ibn 'Umar forbidding cutting the spinal cord (not as invalidation but as dislike) and the athar of Ibn 'Umar, Ibn 'Abbas, and Anas stating that cutting the head is permissible.
The evidence indicates karahah, not tahrim.
5
Note the practical consequence and cross-madhhab difference
In practice, a butcher may inadvertently cut the spinal cord; the meat is halal per Hanafi. Some schools may differ; understand the thamarah al-khilaf.
The mufta bihi is that slaughter is valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۶۰۹] (۳۰) کسی نے چھری حرام مغز تک پہنچادی یا سرکاٹ دیا تو اس کے لئے یہ مکروہ ہے اور اس کا ذبیحہ کھایا جائے گا۔ گلے میں جو ہڈی ہوتی ہے اس کے درمیان میں موٹی رگیں ہوتی ہیں جن کو حرام مغز کہتے ہیں۔ ذبح میں ہڈی تک چھری پہنچانا چاہئے اس سے ذبح مکمل ہو جاتا ہے اس سے زیادہ تکلیف نہیں دینی چاہئے لیکن کسی نے ہڈی کے اندر تک یعنی حرام مغز تک چھری چھودی یا پوری گردن کاٹ دی تو ایسا کرنا مکروہ ہے۔ البتہ ایسا کرنے سے حلقوم ، مری اور ود جان سب کٹ گئے اس لئے ذبیحہ حلال ہو گیا۔ اخبرنی نافع ان ابن عمر نهى عن النخع يقول يقطع مادون العظم ثم يدع حتى يموت (بخاری شریف، باب النحر والذبح ص ۸۲۸ نمبر ۵۵۱۰) عن ابن عباس نهی رسول الله عن الذبيحة ان تفرس قبل ان تموت (سنن بیہقی ، باب کراہیہ التح والفرس ج تاسع ص ۴۷۰ نمبر ۱۹۱۳۶) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ حرام مغز کو توڑنا یا وہاں تک چھری لے جانا مکروہ ہے۔ لیکن ایسا کر لیا تو ذبیحہ حلال ہے۔ وقال ابن عمر وابن عباس وانس اذا قطع الرأس فلا بأس (بخاری شریف، باب النحر والذبح ص ۸۲۸ نمبر۵۵۱۰/ مصنف عبد الرزاق ، باب سنہ الذبیح ج رابع ص ۴۹۰ نمبر ۸۵۹۳) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ سر کٹ جائے یا نخاع تک چھری چلی جائے تو ذبیحہ حلال ہے کوئی حرج کی بات نہیں ہے۔ النخاع : حرام مغز جو گردن کی ہڈی کے درمیان ہوتا ہے۔ سکین : چھری۔
(30) If someone reaches the spinal cord (haram mughz) with the knife or cuts the head, it is makruh for him and his slaughtered animal will be eaten. The neck has a bone; inside it there are thick veins called 'haram mughz' (spinal cord). In slaughter, the knife should reach the bone; this completes the slaughter. One should not cause more pain than that. But if someone inserts the knife inside the bone, i.e., to the spinal cord, or cuts the entire neck, doing so is makruh. However, since doing so cuts the throat (halqum), esophagus (mari'), and jugular veins (wadajan), the slaughtered animal is halal. Nafi' told me that Ibn 'Umar forbade cutting the spinal cord, saying: 'Cut below the bone, then leave it until it dies.' (Bukhari, Bab al-nahr wa al-dhabh, no. 5510) From Ibn 'Abbas: The Messenger of Allah forbade tearing the slaughtered animal before it dies. (Bayhaqi, no. 19136) From this hadith, it is understood that breaking the spinal cord or taking the knife there is makruh. But if one does it, the slaughtered animal is halal. Ibn 'Umar, Ibn 'Abbas, and Anas said: 'If one cuts the head, there is no harm.' (Bukhari, no. 5510; Musannaf 'Abd al-Razzaq, no. 8593) From this athar, it is understood that if the head is cut or the knife reaches the spinal cord, the slaughtered animal is halal; there is no problem. 'Nakh'' means the spinal cord (haram mughz) that is inside the neck bone. 'Sikkīn' means knife.
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage presents ruling (30) concerning cutting the spinal cord (nakh') or severing the head during slaughter. The Hanafi position is that this is makruh tanzihi (disliked) because it unnecessarily prolongs suffering or causes the animal to die before complete bleeding. However, it does not invalidate the slaughter because the essential parts (throat, esophagus, and jugular veins) are cut. The author supports this with hadith from Ibn 'Umar and Ibn 'Abbas, and a report from the Prophet forbidding tearing the animal before it dies. The athar from Ibn 'Umar, Ibn 'Abbas, and Anas confirms that severing the head is permissible and the meat is halal. The key point is that while it is not recommended, it is legally valid.

Key Terms
النخاع (al-nakh'): The spinal cord inside the neck bone; cutting it is makruh.
حرام مغز (haram mughz): The spinal cord (same as nakh')

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person accidentally cuts the spinal cord while slaughtering a goat, what is the ruling according to the Hanafi school?
A) The meat is haram because the spinal cord was cut
B) It is makruh but the meat is halal
C) It is obligatory to repeat the slaughter
D) The meat is halal but the person must pay compensation

Key Takeaway
Cutting the spinal cord or head is makruh but does not invalidate slaughter; the meat remains halal.

Ruling on Slaughtering from the Back of the Neck
Ruling with proof on slaughter from the back of the neck

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on slaughtering from the back of the neck and explain when it is valid versus invalid, citing the evidence from the athar.

Core Idea
Slaughtering from the back is makruh but valid if the four veins are cut while the animal is alive.

This lesson addresses a common scenario: if an animal is slaughtered from the back instead of the front, is the meat halal? The Hanafi school distinguishes based on whether the four essential veins (halqum, mari', wadajan) are severed while the animal is still alive. The author cites two athar from al-Sha'bi and Abi Najih to support this nuanced ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is slaughtering an animal from the back of the neck (qafa). The ruling is makruh tanzih if the veins are cut, but the meat is halal.
2
State the condition for validity
The condition for halal meat is that the animal must be alive and the four essential veins (halqum, mari', and the two wadajan) must be cut before death.
3
Locate the dalil
The author cites two athar: one from al-Sha'bi permitting eating if slaughtered from the back, and another from Abi Najih prohibiting it.
Athar are from Musannaf 'Abd al-Razzaq.
4
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
Al-Sha'bi's athar implies permissibility when veins are cut; Abi Najih's athar indicates prohibition when the animal dies before vein cutting.
5
Reconcile the evidence
The text reconciles by interpreting Abi Najih's prohibition as applying to cases where death occurs before the veins are cut, thus no contradiction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۶۱۰] (۳۱) اگر بکری کو گدی کی طرف سے ذبح کی پس اگر زندہ ہی تھی کہ رگوں کا کاٹ دیا تو جائز ہے اور مکروہ ہے۔ اور اگر رگوں کو کاٹنے سے پہلے مرگئی تو نہیں کھائی جائے گی۔ بکری کو گلے کی جانب سے چھری پھیر کر ذبح کرنا چاہئے تھا لیکن گدی کی جانب سے چھری پھیری اور گلے کی ہڈی کٹی اور حرام مغز کٹا ، پس اگر بکری کے مرنے سے پہلے باقی چار رگیں حلقوم ، مری اور ود جان بھی کٹ گئیں تو بکری حلال ہے۔ اور اگر رگوں کے کٹنے سے پہلے بکری مرگئی تو چونکہ ذبح اختیاری نہیں ہوا اس لئے جانور حرام ہوگا۔ عن الشعبي انه سئل عن ديک ذبح من قبل قفاة فقال ان شئت فكل (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب سنۃ الذبح ج رابع ص۴۹۰ نمبر ۸۵۹۲) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ گدی کی جانب سے ذبح کرے اور تمام رگیں کٹ جائیں تو کھایا جائے گا۔ اور باقی رگیں کٹنے سے پہلے مر گیا تو حلال نہیں اس کے لئے اس اثر سے اشارہ ہے۔ عن ابی نجیح قال من ذبح بعيرا من فلفه متعمدا لم يوكل وان ذبح شاة من فصها متعمدا يعنى الفص متعمدا لم توكل (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب ستة الذبح ج رابع ص ۴۹۱ نمبر ۸۵۹۸) اس اثر کو اس صورت پر محمول کیا جائے گا جب باقی رگیں کٹنے سے پہلے جانور مر گیا ہو۔
(31) If a goat is slaughtered from the back of the neck (qafa), then if it was still alive and the veins were cut, it is permissible but makruh. And if it died before the veins were cut, it will not be eaten. It was required to pass the knife from the throat side, but if one passed it from the back side and the neck bone and spinal cord were cut, then if before the goat died the remaining four veins (halqum, mari', wadajan) were also cut, the goat is halal. And if the goat died before the veins were cut, then since the slaughter was not voluntary, the animal is haram. From al-Sha'bi: He was asked about a rooster slaughtered from the back of the neck, and he said: 'If you wish, eat.' (Musannaf 'Abd al-Razzaq, no. 8592) From this athar, it is understood that if one slaughters from the back and all the veins are cut, it will be eaten. And if it died before the remaining veins were cut, it is not halal; this athar indicates that. From Abi Najih: He said: 'Whoever deliberately slaughters a camel from the back of its neck (falf) is not to be eaten, and if he deliberately slaughters a goat from its back (fas) is not to be eaten.' (Musannaf 'Abd al-Razzaq, no. 8598) This athar is to be interpreted in the case where the animal died before the remaining veins were cut.
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage presents ruling (31) on slaughtering from the back of the neck (qafa). The proper method is to pass the knife across the front of the neck. If one slaughters from the back, it is makruh because it delays the cutting of the essential veins. However, if the animal is still alive and the four required veins (halqum, mari', and the two jugulars) are cut before death, the slaughter is valid and the meat is halal. If the animal dies before these veins are completely severed, the meat is haram because the death was due to injury or strangulation, not proper slaughter. The author cites two athar from al-Sha'bi and Abi Najih to support this distinction: Al-Sha'bi considers it permissible if the veins are cut; Abi Najih's prohibition is interpreted for cases where the animal dies before the veins are cut.

Key Terms
القفا (al-qafa): The back of the neck; slaughtering from there is not the sunnah method.
حلقوم (halqum): The throat (windpipe) - one of the essential veins to cut.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a sheep is slaughtered from the back of the neck and dies before the jugular veins are cut, what is the ruling?
A) The meat is halal
B) The meat is haram
C) It is makruh but halal
D) The slaughter must be repeated

Key Takeaway
Slaughter from the back is valid only if the four veins are cut while the animal is alive; otherwise the meat is haram.

Slaughter Method: Tame Game vs. Wild Domestic Animals
Defines method of slaughter based on current state

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify an animal's current state (tame or wild) and determine the correct method of slaughter (dhabh or hunting) according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Slaughter method follows the animal's current state: tame game requires dhabh; wild domestic requires hunting.

In this lesson, we examine a concise ruling that distinguishes between two scenarios: game animals that become domesticated, and domestic animals that become wild. The principle is that the method of slaughter depends on the animal's present condition, not its origin. This ruling is essential for ensuring lawful meat consumption.

Guided Path
1
Identify the animal's origin
Determine whether the animal is originally game (hunted) or domesticated (livestock). This affects the baseline assumption.
2
Assess its current state
Is the animal tame (accustomed to humans) or wild (untamed)? This is the decisive factor.
Be objective: a tame game animal behaves like livestock; a wild domestic animal behaves like game.
3
Apply the corresponding rule
If the animal is tame game, it must be slaughtered by dhabh (throat cutting). If it is a wild domestic animal, it must be killed by hunting (striking with spear, bullet, etc.).
The method is wajib for the meat to be halal.
4
Confirm by noting any exceptions
The margin notes mention that cutting the head is allowed by some companions, but the standard rule stands. For detailed exceptions, refer to other rulings.
These notes do not override the main ruling for typical cases.

(32) For game that becomes tame, its method of slaughter (zakah) is dhabh (throat cutting). And for domesticated animals that become wild, their method of slaughter is striking with a spear and wounding (i.e., like hunting). Marginal notes: (a) The Prophet forbade tearing the slaughtered animal before it dies. (b) Ibn 'Abbas, Ibn 'Umar, and Anas said: 'If one cuts the head, there is no harm.' (c) Al-Sha'bi was asked about a rooster slaughtered from the side of the neck, and he said: 'If you wish, eat.' (d) Abi Najih said: 'Whoever deliberately slaughters a camel from the side of the neck, it is not to be eaten; and if he deliberately slaughters a goat from its back side (anas), it is not to be eaten.'
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage presents ruling (32) which addresses two scenarios: (1) A wild animal (sayd) that becomes tame (domesticated) – its slaughter method is dhabh (cutting the throat), because it is now like a domestic animal. (2) A domesticated animal (like a cow or goat) that becomes wild and cannot be caught easily – its slaughter method is that of hunting: striking it with a spear or bullet where possible, similar to game animals. This is based on the principle that the method follows the animal's current state: tame animals require dhabh, wild animals require wounding. The margin notes provide additional supporting statements from the Prophet and the Salaf, but these are references already discussed in earlier rulings.

Key Terms
زكاة (zakah): The method of making an animal lawful (slaughter or hunting).
مانوس (ma'nus): Tame (accustomed to humans).
وحشی (wahshi): Wild (not tame).

Ruling on Slaughtering from the Back of the Neck
Ruling on slaughtering from the back: conditions and karahah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on slaughtering from the back of the neck, identify the essential conditions for halal meat, and evaluate the evidence for karahah.

Core Idea
Slaughtering from the back is makruh, but the meat is halal if the four veins are cut while alive.

This lesson examines a classic Hanafi ruling on slaughtering an animal from the back of the neck (qafa). In Hanafi fiqh, the method is considered makruh tanzihi (slightly disliked) due to potential resemblance to pre-Islamic practices or causing additional pain. However, the meat remains halal provided the animal was alive when the four essential veins were severed. The passage cites several prophetic hadith and companion athar to support this nuanced position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Identify the specific act being ruled upon: slaughtering a sheep from the back of the neck. Determine the hukm level for the act and the resulting meat.
The act is makruh tanzih, but the meat is halal if conditions are met.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the proofs cited: hadith from Ibn Abbas (prohibition of tearing before death), athar from Ibn Umar, Anas, al-Sha'bi, and Abi Najih.
These are found in Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Sahih al-Bukhari, and Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Understand how each proof supports the ruling. The hadith implies karahah for cutting the spinal cord prematurely. The athar indicate that cutting the head or spinal cord is not inherently haram as long as the veins are cut while alive.
The karahah is derived from the prohibition; the permissibility from the companion statements.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Recognize that some scholars might consider it haram if the spinal cord is cut. The Hanafi position distinguishes between the act and the outcome.
Cross-madhhab: Shafi'i also considers it makruh, Hanbali may allow without karahah in necessity.
5
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: in Hanafi law, the meat is halal and can be eaten, though the method is discouraged. Other views might prohibit the meat.
This affects fatwa and daily practice.

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on slaughtering an animal from the back of the neck (qafa). The core ruling: if the animal remains alive long enough for the four essential veins (hulqum, mari', wadajayn) to be cut, the meat is halal, though the method is makruh (disliked). If the animal dies before the veins are cut, it is not halal. The author cites hadith from Ibn Abbas, Ibn Umar, Anas, al-Sha'bi, and Abi Najih to support that cutting the head or spinal cord does not render the meat haram as long as the veins are cut while alive. The karahah is due to resembling pre-Islamic practices or causing unnecessary pain. The Hanafi position permits the meat but considers the method makruh tanzihi (slightly disliked), not haram.

Key Terms
النخاع (al-nukha'): The spinal cord (haram mughz), the white cord inside the vertebrae of the neck.
قفا (qafa): The back of the neck, opposite the throat.
العروق (al-'uruq): The four essential veins: hulqum (windpipe), mari' (esophagus), and two wadajayn (jugular veins).

Key Takeaway
Slaughtering from the back is makruh, but the meat remains halal provided the four essential veins were cut while the animal was still alive.

Tame Game and Wild Domesticated Animals: Slaughter Methods
Ruling with proof on slaughter methods

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the required slaughter method for tame game and wild domesticated animals, and apply the ruling based on the animal's condition.

Core Idea
A tame wild animal must be slaughtered by dhabh; a wild domestic animal may be wounded if it cannot be caught.

This lesson examines a key Hanafi ruling regarding the method of slaughter when an animal's nature has changed. Wild animals that become tame are treated like livestock, requiring dhabh (throat cutting). Conversely, domesticated animals that become wild and unattainable may be killed by 'aqr (wounding), similar to hunting. We will explore the textual proofs from the Sunnah and the underlying principle of necessity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories
Note the two conditions: (1) Tame game (musta'nis min al-sayd) and (2) Wild livestock (mutawahhish min al-na'am). Each has its own ruling.
2
State the ruling for each
For tame game: dhabh is required. For wild livestock: 'aqr (wounding) suffices when the animal cannot be caught. Also note that for camels, nahr is preferred but dhabh is permissible.
3
Examine the proof from the first hadith
The hadith of Adi ibn Hatim: 'If you release your dog and it catches game, and you find it alive, slaughter it (fadhabbahu).' This shows that when the animal is under control, dhabh is commanded.
4
Examine the proof from the second hadith
The hadith of Rafi' ibn Khadij: a camel bolted and was killed by an arrow. The Prophet said, 'These animals have wild tendencies like wild beasts, so if one escapes you, do with it like this.' This permits 'aqr for domesticated animals that become wild and cannot be caught.
5
Apply the underlying principle
Necessity permits the alternative. When an animal is tame and catchable, dhabh is obligatory. When wild and uncatchable, 'aqr is permissible. The ruling is a mercy that avoids making meat haram due to impossibility.
This reflects the Hanafi principle that dire necessity (darurah) allows otherwise prohibited means of slaughter.

And what becomes tame from game, its slaughter is dhabh; and what becomes wild from domesticated animals, its slaughter is 'aqr (wounding) and injury. [2612] (33) And the preferred for camels is nahr, but if he slaughters (dhabh) it is permissible. Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the method of slaughter for animals that have changed their nature. The core rule: if a wild animal (sayd) becomes tame (musta'nis), its method of slaughter becomes dhabh (throat cutting) like domesticated animals. Conversely, if a domesticated animal (na'am) becomes wild (mutawahhish) such that it cannot be caught, its slaughter is 'aqr (wounding by arrow or spear) like game. The text provides two hadith: (1) from Adi ibn Hatim: the Prophet ordered to slaughter (dhabh) a game if found alive; (2) from Rafi' ibn Khadij: the Prophet allowed killing a bolting camel with an arrow. The Hanafi position: in necessity, 'aqr suffices for a domestic animal that cannot be caught, but if it can be caught, dhabh is required. The underlying principle is that necessity permits the alternative method.

Key Terms
استئناس (isti'nas): Becoming tame, accustomed to humans.
توحش (tawahhush): Becoming wild, escaping human control.
العقر (al-'aqr): Wounding, shooting with arrow or spear to kill.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) It must be caught and slaughtered by dhabh.
B) It can be killed by shooting an arrow ( 'aqr).
C) It cannot be slaughtered, so the meat is wasted.
D) Only dhabh is valid, regardless of the situation.

Key Takeaway
The method of slaughter depends on the animal's current state: tame game requires dhabh; wild domestic allows 'aqr in necessity.
