Preferred Method for Camel: Nahr over Dhabh
Ruling with proof on the preferred slaughter method for camels

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the preferred method of slaughter for camels and explain why nahr is recommended while dhabh is permissible but disliked, citing the Quranic and prophetic proofs.

Core Idea
A camel should be slaughtered by nahr (chest cut), not dhabh (throat cut); dhabh is valid but disliked.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling on the method of slaughter for camels. The text distinguishes between nahr (cutting the lower neck) and dhabh (throat cutting). While dhabh is the standard method for most animals, camels have a special recommendation for nahr. We will look at the textual proofs from Quran and Sunnah that establish this preference, and why dhabh is still permissible.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling on camel slaughter
Identify the hukm level for nahr and dhabh. Nahr is mustahabb (sunnah muakkadah), dhabh is ja'iz but makruh.
The text explicitly says: 'والمستحب في الابل النحر وان ذبحها جاز' – 'The preferred in camels is nahr, and if he slaughters it (dhabh), it is permissible [but disliked].'
2
Identify the primary proof from Quran
Locate the Quranic verse cited: 'فصل لربك وانحر' (So pray to your Lord and sacrifice [nahr]). Explain how this verse indicates nahr for camels.
The imperative 'wanhar' is understood by Hanafis to refer to camel sacrifice by nahr, as the context of Surah al-Kawthar relates to sacrificial animals.
3
Identify the secondary proof from Sunnah
Find the hadith from Hajjat al-Wada' where the Prophet sacrificed 63 camels by nahr. How does this demonstrate the recommendation?
The Prophet's action sets the sunnah – although nahr is not obligatory, his practice makes it recommended (mustahabb).
4
Analyze the ruling's scope and cross-madhhab dispute
Note that some schools (e.g., Maliki) consider nahr obligatory for camels. Understand why Hanafis consider it only recommended.
Hanafis interpret the Quranic command as indicative of preference, not obligation, due to the principle that commands can be for recommendation (nadb) rather than obligation (wujub).

کر دے یعنی پکڑنے نہ دے تو اس کے ساتھ یہی معاملہ کرو یعنی تیر سے مار کر ذبح کر دو تو حلال ہو جائے گا (ج) اپنے رب کے لئے نماز پڑھئے اور ذبح کیجئے۔
Al-Sharh al-Thamiri Part 4, page 25, Book of Hunting. And what becomes wild from domesticated animals, its slaughter is 'aqr and wounding [2612] (33). And the preferred in camels is nahr, and if he slaughters it (dhabh), it is permissible and disliked. (Then Urdu commentary including the ayah 'fasalli lirabbika wanhar' and hadith about the Prophet sacrificing 63 camels at Hajj.)
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the preferred method of slaughter for camels. The core ruling: for camels, nahr (cutting the lower neck, just above the chest) is mustahabb (recommended). If one instead performs dhabh (throat cutting), it is permissible (ja'iz) but makruh (disliked). The proof cited is the Quranic verse 'fasalli lirabbika wanhar' (So pray to your Lord and sacrifice [nahr]) from Surah al-Kawthar, and the practice of the Prophet in Hajjat al-Wada' where he sacrificed 63 camels by nahr. The Hanafi position thus favors nahr for camels, but dhabh is not invalid. This is specific to camels; for other animals, dhabh is the norm.

Key Terms
النحر (al-nahr): Slaughtering a camel by cutting the lower neck (near the chest), distinct from dhabh.
الذبح (al-dhabh): Slaughtering by cutting the throat (hulqum and mari') for sheep, goats, cows, etc.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on slaughtering a camel by dhabh (throat cutting)?
A) It is invalid and the meat is haram.
B) It is permissible but disliked (makruh).
C) It is the recommended method (sunnah).
D) It is obligatory to perform nahr instead.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, nahr is the recommended method for slaughtering camels, while dhabh is permissible but disliked.

Nahr: The Recommended Slaughter Method for Camels
Ruling plus proof for camel slaughter method

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on camel slaughter methods and identify the Quranic and hadith proofs that establish nahr as mustahabb and dhabh as makruh tanzihan.

Core Idea
Nahr (cutting at the neck base) is recommended for camels; dhabh (throat-cutting) is permissible but disliked.

In this passage, we learn that camels have a specific recommended slaughter method distinct from other animals. The author cites the Quran, the Prophet's practice, and narrations from Companions to show that nahr is mustahabb for camels, while dhabh is valid but makruh tanzihan. Understanding this distinction is essential for proper application of Islamic slaughter rules.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
Read the opening sentence: 'والمستحب في الإبل النحر' (the recommended method for camels is nahr). Note that dhabh is said to be permissible but disliked.
The ruling is clear: nahr is mustahabb, dhabh is makruh.
2
Locate the Primary Proof
The author first cites Quran 108:2: 'فصل لربك وانحر' (So pray to your Lord and sacrifice). The imperative 'wanhar' is used to recommend nahr.
In Hanafi usul, al-amr (imperative) indicates recommendation (nadb) unless there is evidence of obligation.
3
Analyze the Secondary Proofs
Several hadith are presented: the hadith of Adi ibn Hatim shows that dhabh is used for captured game, not camels; the hadith of Rafi' shows that a wild camel can be killed by shooting (aqr), which is a form of nahr; the Prophet's own act of nahr at Hajj confirms the practice; and the athar from al-Zuhri and Qatada states that both methods are permissible for camels and cattle.
These proofs collectively support the preference of nahr for camels while acknowledging dhabh as valid.
4
Note the Cross-Madhhab Difference
The Hanafi school distinguishes between camels (nahr recommended) and other animals (dhabh recommended). Some other schools may treat all animals alike, preferring dhabh for all.
The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) is that a person who slaughters a camel by dhabh has valid meat but commits a disliked act in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
النعم فذكاته العقر والجرح. والمستحب في الإبل النحر، وإن ذبحها جاز ويكره. قال الله تعالى: فصل لربك وانحر. عن عدي بن حاتم قال قال لي رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: إذا أرسلت كلبك فاذكر اسم الله، فإن أمسك عليك فأدركته حيا فاذبحه. (رواه مسلم) وعن رافع بن خديج قال: كنا مع النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم في سفر فند بعير من الإبل فرماه رجل بسهم فحبسه، فقال: إن لها أوابد كأوابد الوحش، فما غلبكم منها فاصنعوا به هكذا. (رواه البخاري وأبو داود) وفي حجة الوداع: ثم انصرف إلى المنحر فنحر ثلاثا وستين بيده. (رواه مسلم) وعن الزهري وقتادة قالا: الإبل والبقر إن شئت ذبحت وإن شئت نحرت. (مصنف عبد الرزاق)
For cattle, its slaughter is by wounding and cutting. The recommended method for camels is nahr, and if he slaughters (dhabh) it, it is permissible but disliked. Allah says: 'So pray to your Lord and sacrifice (nahr).' From Adi ibn Hatim: The Messenger of Allah said to me: When you send your dog, mention the name of Allah; if it catches for you and you find it alive, then slaughter it (dhabh). (Reported by Muslim). From Rafi' ibn Khadij: We were with the Prophet on a journey when a camel became wild, so a man shot it with an arrow and stopped it. He said: 'Camels have wildness like wild animals, so whatever overpowers you, do with it thus.' (Reported by Bukhari and Abu Dawud). And in the Farewell Pilgrimage: Then he went to the place of sacrifice and sacrificed (nahr) sixty-three camels with his own hand. (Reported by Muslim). From al-Zuhri and Qatada: They said, 'Camels and cattle, if you wish you may slaughter (dhabh) and if you wish you may sacrifice (nahr).' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq)
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the method of slaughtering camels. The author states that the recommended method for camels is 'nahr' (cutting at the base of the neck), but if one performs 'dhabh' (cutting the throat), it is still permissible, though disliked. The proof includes the Quranic verse 'fasarli lirabbika wanhar' which indicates nahr is preferred, and numerous hadith: the hadith of Adi ibn Hatim instructs that if a hunted animal is caught alive, it must be slaughtered (dhabh), not nahr. The hadith of Rafi' ibn Khadij shows that if a domestic camel becomes wild and cannot be caught, it can be killed with an arrow, which is a form of 'aqr' (wounding). The Prophet's own practice of nahr in the Farewell Pilgrimage confirms its recommendation. The athar from al-Zuhri and Qatada states that both methods are permissible for both camels and cattle. The overall Hanafi position is that nahr is mustahabb for camels, and dhabh is makruh tanzihan (disliked but the meat is halal). The commentary also explains the distinction between 'dhabh ikhtiyari' (voluntary slaughter) and 'dhabh idtirari' (emergency slaughter).

Key Terms
النحر (an-nahr): Cutting at the base of the neck, specifically for camels.
الذبح (adh-dhabh): Cutting the throat, slicing the trachea and esophagus.
العقر (al-`aqr): Wounding or injuring; in this context, a method of slaughtering camels by cutting at the base of the neck (nahr).
الجرح (al-jarh): Cutting; in this context, referring to dhabh (throat-cutting).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the recommended method (mustahabb) for slaughtering a camel according to the Hanafi school?
A) Dhabh (cutting the throat)
B) Nahr (cutting the base of the neck)
C) Wounding with an arrow
D) Any method is equally preferred

Key Takeaway
Nahr is the recommended method for slaughtering camels; dhabh is valid but disliked.

The Recommended Method for Slaughtering Cows and Goats: Dhabh vs. Nahr
Ruling with proof on the method of slaughter for cows and goats.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on slaughtering cows and goats and distinguish the recommended method (dhabh) from the permissible but disliked method (nahr).

Core Idea
For cows and goats, dhabh is recommended; nahr is valid but disliked.

This passage clarifies the Hanafi position on the method of slaughter for cows and goats. While both dhabh (throat-cutting) and nahr (base-of-neck-cutting) are valid, dhabh is the preferred method based on Quranic usage and Prophetic practice. Understanding this distinction is essential for proper slaughter according to the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The passage rules on the method of slaughtering cows and goats. The recommended method is dhabh, while nahr is permissible but makruh.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites Quran 2:71, which uses the verb 'dhabh' for the cow, and three ahadith: one about sharing a cow in tamattu', one about the Prophet slaughtering a ram, and one about the Prophet performing nahr for his wives.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Quranic verse shows that dhabh was the method for the cow. The hadith of Jabir about tamattu' confirms that a cow was slaughtered by dhabh. The hadith of Aisha shows that nahr is also performed on cows (the Prophet did nahr for his wives), which indicates permissibility. The overall evidence supports dhabh as the sunnah.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some scholars hold that nahr is also recommended for cows, but the Hanafi school distinguishes by species: dhabh for cows/goats, nahr for camels.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that dhabh is mustahabb for cows and goats, while nahr is makruh tanzihan. This is based on the explicit Quranic term and the practice of the Companions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمستحب في البقر والغنم الذبح، فإن نحرهما جاز ويكره. قال الله تعالى: فذبحوها وما كادوا يفعلون. عن جابر بن عبد الله قال: كنا نتمتع في عهد رسول الله نذبح البقرة عن سبعة نشترك فيها. (رواه أبو داود) وعن جابر بن عبد الله قال: شهدت مع رسول الله الأضحى في المصلى فلما قضى خطبته نزل من منبره وأتى بكبش فذبحه رسول الله بيده. (رواه أبو داود والنسائي) وعن عائشة قالت: دخل علينا يوم النحر بلحم بقر فقلت ما هذا؟ قال: نحر رسول الله عن أزواجه. (رواه البخاري)
The recommended method for cows and goats is dhabh (throat-cutting). If one does nahr on them, it is permissible but disliked. Allah says: 'So they slaughtered her, though they almost did not.' (Quran 2:71) From Jabir ibn Abdullah: We used to perform tamattu' in the time of the Messenger of Allah and slaughter a cow on behalf of seven people, sharing it. (Reported by Abu Dawud) From Jabir ibn Abdullah: I was present with the Messenger of Allah at the Eid al-Adha prayer. When he finished his sermon, he came down from the minbar and was brought a ram. Then the Messenger of Allah slaughtered it with his own hand. (Reported by Abu Dawud and al-Nasa'i) From Aisha: She said, 'On the day of al-Nahr, meat of a cow was brought to us. I asked, "What is this?" He said, "The Messenger of Allah sacrificed (nahr) on behalf of his wives."' (Reported by Bukhari)
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the method of slaughtering cows and goats. The author states that the recommended method for cows and goats is dhabh (cutting the throat), but if one performs nahr (cutting at the base of the neck), it is still permissible, though disliked. The proof includes a Quranic verse about the cow of the Children of Israel which uses the verb 'dhabh'. The hadith from Jabir about tamattu' shows that a cow was slaughtered (dhabh) for seven people. Another hadith from Jabir shows that the Prophet slaughtered a ram (dhabh) with his own hand. The hadith from Aisha shows that the Prophet performed nahr on a cow on behalf of his wives, indicating that nahr is also valid for cows. The Hanafi position is that dhabh is mustahabb for cows and goats, and nahr is makruh tanzihan. The commentary also notes that cows and goats are different from camels in this ruling.

Key Terms
الذبح (adh-dhabh): Cutting the throat, slicing the trachea and esophagus.
النحر (an-nahr): Cutting at the base of the neck, specifically for camels; for cows/goats it is valid but disliked.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling for slaughtering a goat?
A) Only dhabh is valid, nahr is haram.
B) Dhabh is recommended, nahr is permissible but disliked.
C) Both dhabh and nahr are equally recommended.
D) Nahr is recommended, dhabh is disliked.

Key Takeaway
For cows and goats, dhabh is the sunnah; nahr is permissible but disliked according to the Hanafi school.

Ruling on Fetus Found Dead in a Slaughtered Animal
States the ruling on fetus found dead in slaughtered animal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a dead fetus found in a slaughtered animal and explain why the mother's slaughter does not extend to the fetus.

Core Idea
A dead fetus found in a slaughtered animal is not halal; it died from suffocation, not slaughter.

This lesson addresses a specific scenario in animal slaughter: when a pregnant animal is slaughtered and the fetus is found dead inside. The Hanafi school has a clear ruling that such a fetus is not permissible to eat. This lesson will examine the reasoning and evidence behind this position, including the response to differing views.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act described is finding a dead fetus inside a slaughtered animal. The ruling (hukm) is that it is not to be eaten – it is haram.
The ruling is unconditional regardless of fetal development (hair or no hair).
2
Understand the reasoning
The fetus is a separate life from its mother. The mother's slaughter only takes effect on her own life, not on the fetus. The fetus died from suffocation after the mother's death, not from the slaughter act itself. Therefore, it is considered carrion (maytah).
This reasoning distinguishes between the direct effect of slaughter and indirect causes of death.
3
Examine the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi school cites the athar of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i: 'The slaughter of one life does not serve as slaughter for two lives.' This supports the view that each animal requires its own slaughter.
This is a transmission from the tabi'in, indicating early support for the ruling.
4
Consider the opposing views
Imam al-Shafi'i and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that the mother's slaughter renders the fetus halal, based on the hadith of Jabir: 'ذكوة الجنين ذكوة امه' (The slaughter of the fetus is the slaughter of its mother).
The Hanafi response interprets this hadith as referring to a fetus already dead at the time of maternal slaughter, or considers it abrogated or specific.
5
Conclude the mufta bihi
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the Hanafi school is that the dead fetus is not halal, regardless of hair development. This is the view of Abu Hanifa and is supported by the athar of Ibrahim, and is the position of the matn.
This position is from Zahir al-Riwayah and is the basis for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن نحر ناقة او ذبح بقرة او شاة فوجد في بطنها جنينا ميتا لم يوكل اشعر او لم يشعر۔ كسي نے اونٹنی نحر کی يا گائے يا بکری ذبح کی اور ان کے پیٹ میں مردہ بچہ پایا تو نہیں کھایا جائے گا بال آگئے ہوں يا نہ آئے ہوں۔ اونٹنی نحر کی اور اس کے پیٹ سے مردہ بچہ نکلا يا گائے ذبح کی يا بکری ذبح کی اور ان کے پیٹ سے مردہ بچہ نکلا تو چاہے بچہ اتنا بڑا ہو گيا ہو کہ اس کے جسم پر بال اگ آئے ہوں تب بھی اس بچے کو نہیں کھایا جائے گا۔ اس لئے کہ بچہ اگر چہ ماں کے ساتھ متصل ہے لیکن اس کا جسم بالکل الگ ہے ماں کے ذبيح کرنے سے بچے کا ذبيح نہیں ہوگا، وہ زندہ باہر نکلتا تو الگ سے ذبح کر کے حلال کرتے اور مردہ باہر نکلا تو سانس گھٹنے کی وجہ سے مرا ہے ماں کو ذبح کرنے کی وجہ سے نہیں مرا ہے اس لئے اس کو نہیں کھایا جائے گا (۲) اثر میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ عن ابراهيم قال لا تكون زكوة نفس زكوة نفسين يعني ان الجنين اذا ذبحت امه لم يوكل حتى يدرك زكاته (الف) ( كتاب الآثار امام محمد، باب زکوة الجنين والعقیقہ ص ۷۸ انمبر ۸۰۸) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ ماں کے ذبح کرنے سے بچہ ذبح نہیں ہوگا چاہے بال اگ آئے ہوں یا نہ اگے ہوں۔ اننده امام شافعی اور صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ ماں کے ذبح کرنے سے بچے کا ذبيح ہو جائے گا اس لئے بچے کو بھی کھایا جا سکتا ہے۔ اور ایک روایت میں ہے کہ بچے کو بال آگئے ہوں اور مکمل بچہ ہو چکا ہو تو کھایا جاسکتا ہے۔ حدیث میں ہے۔ عن جابر بن عبد الله عن رسول الله الله الله قال ذكوة الجنين ذكوة امه(ب) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب ما جاء فی ذکوة الجنین ص ۳۴ نمبر ۲۸۲۸ متر مندی شریف، باب ماجاء فی ذکرة الجنین ص ۲۷۲ نمبر ۱۴۷۶) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ ماں کے ذبح کرنے سے بچہ بھی ذبح ہو جائے گا اور حلال ہو جائے گا۔ اور بال اگے تب حلال ہو گا اس کی دلیل۔ عن الزهري قال في الجنين اذا اشعر او وبر فذكوته ذكوة امه (ج) (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب الجنین ج رابع ص ۵۰۰ نمبر ۶۴۰ ۸ / موطا امام مالک، باب زکوۃ مافی نطن الذبیہ ص ۴۹۰) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ بال اگے ہوں تو کھایا جائے گا ورنہ نہیں۔ ت جنین : ماں کے پیٹ کا بچہ۔ وبر : اونٹ کا بال۔ حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت ابراہیم نے فرمایا ایک جان کے ذبح کرنے سے دو جانوں کا ذبح نہیں ہو گا یعنی جب بچے کی ماں ذبيح کی جائے تو پیٹ کا بچہ نہیں کھایا جائے گا جب تک کہ خود اس کو ذبح نہ کرے (ب) آپ نے فرمایا ماں کے ذبح کرنے سے خود پیٹ کا بچہ بھی ذبيح ہو جائے گا (ج) پیٹ کے بچے کے بارے میں حضرت زہری نے فرمایا اگر بال آجائے تو مان کے ذبح کرنے سے بچے کا ذبيح ہو جائے گا۔
Whoever slaughters a she-camel or slaughters a cow or a sheep and finds in its belly a dead fetus, it is not to be eaten, whether it has hair or not.
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This is a ruling from the Hanafi school concerning the edibility of a fetus found dead after its mother has been slaughtered. The matn states that such a fetus is not permissible to eat regardless of whether it has grown hair (a sign of full development) or not. The commentary explains the reasoning: the fetus, although physically connected to the mother, is a separate life. The mother's slaughter only takes effect on her own life; it does not extend to the fetus. The fetus died due to suffocation after the mother's death, not directly from the slaughter. Therefore, it is considered carrion (maytah). The Hanafi position is supported by an athar from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i who said that the slaughter of one life does not serve as slaughter for two lives. The commentary then mentions that Imam al-Shafi'i and the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, though here 'Sahibayn' likely refers to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad but they are actually Hanafi) hold a different view: they consider the fetus to be rendered halal by the mother's slaughter. Some narrations differentiate based on whether the fetus is hairless or fully haired. The commentary includes a hadith from Jabir that the slaughter of the fetus is the slaughter of its mother, which the Shafi'is use as proof. However, the Hanafis interpret this hadith as referring to the fetus that is already dead at the time of slaughter, not alive, or they consider it abrogated or specific. The Hanafis also cite an athar from al-Zuhri that the fetus is halal only if it has hair, but this is not the relied-upon position. The relied-upon Hanafi view is that the fetus is not halal, as established in Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
جنين (janīn): The unborn offspring in the womb of a slaughtered animal.
ذكوة (dhakāt): The act of lawful slaughter.
اشعر (ash‘ara): To become hairy; refers to the fetus developing body hair.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on eating a dead fetus found inside a slaughtered sheep?
A) It is halal if the fetus has hair.
B) It is halal because the mother's slaughter suffices for it.
C) It is not halal, whether it has hair or not.
D) It is halal only if the fetus is alive and then slaughtered separately.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a dead fetus from a slaughtered animal is not edible; it requires its own separate slaughter to be halal.

Prohibition of Eating Predatory Animals and Birds
States the prohibition of eating fanged beasts and clawed birds.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on eating fanged beasts and clawed birds, identify the primary dalil, and explain the rationale for prohibition.

Core Idea
Eating fanged beasts and clawed birds is haram due to explicit prophetic prohibition.

This lesson establishes a clear-cut prohibition in the Hanafi school: any animal with fangs used for tearing prey or any bird with claws used for catching prey is haram for consumption. The ruling is grounded in a prophetic hadith, and the commentary explains the rationale behind it, emphasizing the importance of avoiding such foods. You will learn to identify these animals and understand the evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is consuming animals classified as 'dhū nāb' (fanged beasts) and 'dhū mikhleb' (clawed birds). The ruling is taḥrīm (prohibition).
2
Locate the dalīl
The evidence is a ḥadīth from Ibn ‘Abbās (raḍiyallāhu ‘anhumā) that the Prophet (ṣallallāhu ‘alayhi wa sallam) forbade eating every fanged beast and every clawed bird.
The ḥadīth is found in Muslim, Abū Dāwūd, and Bukhārī.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalālah
The word 'nahā' (forbade) indicates a prohibition. The phrase 'kull dhī nāb min al-sibā‘' is general ('āmm) and includes all such animals, making the ruling comprehensive.
In Hanafi uṣūl, the general command of prohibition (al-nahy) indicates that the act is ḥarām.
4
Note the ʿillah (reason)
The commentary mentions two reasons: first, consuming such animals may instill aggressive traits (ta’thīr fī al-akhlāq), and second, these animals are considered impure or harmful (najis/muḍirr).
The ʿillah supports the prohibition even though the ḥadīth itself does not state a reason explicitly.
5
Consider cross-madhhab differences
Although the prohibition is agreed upon, there is ikhtilāf on specific animals, e.g., the hyena. The Ḥanafī school includes all fanged beasts, while some other schools exclude certain ones.
This does not affect the general ruling that fanged beasts are ḥarām in the Ḥanafī madhhab.

Source Text

It is not permissible to eat every fanged beast nor every clawed bird.
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage states a clear prohibition in the Hanafi school against eating predatory animals (those with fangs) and predatory birds (those with claws). The commentary explains that these animals use their sharp teeth or talons to tear and kill other creatures. The reason for prohibition is both to avoid acquiring their aggressive nature and because these animals are generally considered impure or harmful. The proof is a hadith from Ibn Abbas that the Prophet (peace be upon him) forbade eating every fanged beast and every clawed bird. The commentary defines 'ناب' as sharp canine teeth and 'مخلب' as claw. The prohibition is based on the explicit text of the hadith, and it is a matter of consensus among the schools, though there are differences in details (e.g., hyena).

Key Terms
ذو ناب (dhū nāb): Any animal with canine fangs used for tearing flesh; predator.
ذو مخلب (dhū mikhleb): Any bird with claws (talons) used for catching and tearing prey.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary evidence for the prohibition of eating fanged beasts in the Hanafi school?
A) A Quranic verse stating 'do not eat predators'.
B) A hadith from Ibn Abbas forbidding every fanged beast and clawed bird.
C) Consensus of the Companions.
D) Analogy to the impurity of blood.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling that eating fanged beasts and clawed birds is haram is firmly based on the general prohibition in the hadith, with the rationale of avoiding harmful or predatory traits.

Ruling on Eating the Field Crow: Halal Among Crows
Permits eating a specific type of crow that does not eat carrion or filth.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on eating the field crow, distinguish it from other types of crows using the proofs from hadith and athar, and explain the reasoning behind its permissibility.

Core Idea
The field crow is halal because it does not eat carrion or filth, unlike other crows.

Many Muslims encounter crows and wonder about their legal status. The Hanafi school provides a detailed ruling based on the bird's diet and behavior, distinguishing between predatory crows, carrion-eating crows, and the field crow that feeds on grains and insects. This lesson unpacks the proofs and classifications so you can understand why one type is permissible and others are not.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its category
The passage begins by stating 'there is no harm in eating the field crow'. This indicates a ruling of permissibility (mubah). Note that this is a specific exception to the general rule that crows are haram.
The ruling is not general for all crows; it is specific to ghurab al-zar‘.
2
Distinguish the three types of crows
The commentary classifies crows into three types: (1) predatory crow with hooked beak, (2) carrion-eating crow (dirt crow), (3) field crow that eats grains and insects. Each has a different ruling based on its nature.
Only the third type is halal.
3
Apply the hadith on predatory birds and jallalah
The first type is haram due to the hadith forbidding every clawed bird (kullu dhi mikhleb min al-tayr). The second type is haram by analogy to the jallalah (animal that eats filth) based on the hadith prohibiting consumption of jallalah meat and milk.
The field crow avoids both characteristics, so it falls outside the prohibition.
4
Apply the athar from Ibrahim on carrion-eating birds
An athar from Ibrahim (al-Nakha‘i) states that any bird that eats carrion is makruh (or haram). This further supports the prohibition of the second type.
The field crow does not eat carrion, so this athar does not apply.
5
Conclude why the field crow is halal
Combining the proofs: the field crow is not predatory and does not eat carrion or filth. Therefore, it is permissible. The Hanafi school holds this view, distinguishing it from other schools that may consider all crows haram.
This is a classic example of istithna' (exception) based on specific characteristics.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا بأس باكل غراب الزرع . کوئی حرج کی بات نہیں ہے کھیتی کے کوے کھانے میں ۔ تین قسم کے کوے ہوتے ہیں اور اردو میں تینوں کو کو کہتے ہیں (۱) ایک وہ کو جس کی چونچ تیز ہوتی ہے اور مڑی ہوئی ہوتی ہے اس کے کالے میں تھوڑی سفیدی مائل ہوتی ہے۔ یہ بہت ہوشیار پرندہ ہوتا ہے۔ یہ ہمارے یہاں گھروں پر آکر مرغی کا چھوٹا بچہ لے بھاگتا ہے اور پھاڑ کھاتا ہے۔ یہ کوا اوپر کی حدیث عن ابن عباس قال نهى رسول الله له الا الله عن اكل كل ذي ناب من السبع وعن كل ذى مخلب من الطير (ب) (مسلم شریف نمبر ۱۹۳۴ ابوداؤد شریف، نمبر ۳۸۰۳) کی وجہ سے حرام ہوگا ۔ کیونکہ یہ پھاڑ کھانے والا پرندہ ہے۔ دوسرا کو بالکل کا لا ہوتا ہے۔ یہ پہلے کوے کی طرح ہوشیار نہیں ہوتا اور نہ یہ شکار کر سکتا ہے۔ اس کو ہم لوگ بہار میں ڈرکوا کہتے ہیں۔ یہ ہر وقت گو بریالید بکھیر بکھیر کر اس سے دانہ نکال کر کھاتا رہتا ہے۔ یہ مردہ گوشت بھی کھا لیتا ہے۔ اس لئے یہ بھی حرام ہے۔ عن ابراهيم انه كره من الطير كل شيء يأكل الميتة (ج) (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب الغراب والحداة ج رابع ص ۵۱۹ نمبر ۸۷۰۳ر مصنف ابن ابی شیبة ۳۷ ماشنہی عن الكله من الطيور والسباع ، ج رابع ص ۲۶۳ نمبر ۱۹۸۶۵) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ جو مردہ کھاتا ہو وہ مکروہ ہے (۲) اگر اونٹ گندگی کھائے تو اس کا گوشت کھانا بھی درست نہیں اسلئے کو گندگی کھائے تو بدرجہ اولی اس کا کھانا درست نہیں ہوگا۔ حدیث میں ہے۔ عن ابن عمر قال نھی رسول الله ولي الله عن اكل الجلالة والبانها (د) (ابوداؤد شریف ، باب انھی عن اكل الجلالۃ والبا نھاج ثانی ص ۷۵ انمبر ۳۷۸۵) ڈرکو گندگی کھاتا ہے اور مردہ جانور کا گوشت بھی کھاتا ہے اس لئے وہ بھی حلال نہیں ہے۔ تیسرے قسم کا کو انگلینڈ میں دیکھ وہ بالکل کالا ہوتا ہے اور عام چڑیوں کی طرح بھرا ہوتا ہے اور کھیتوں میں دانہ چگتا رہتا ہے اور کوڑے مکوڑے کھاتا رہتا ہے اس کا نام ہر ملک میں الگ الگ ہے۔ لیکن یہی غراب الزرع کھیتی کا کوا ہے۔ چونکہ یہ نہ مردار کھاتا ہے اور نہ گندگی میں منہ ڈالتا ہے اس لئے یہ حلال ہے۔
There is no harm in eating the field crow.
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage discusses the permissibility of eating a specific type of crow called 'ghurab al-zar‘' (field crow). The commentary classifies crows into three types. The first type is predatory with a hooked beak, steals chicks, and is haram based on the hadith forbidding clawed birds. The second type is the 'dirt crow' (often called 'dharam kauwa') that eats carrion and filth, making it haram by analogy to the jallalah animals (which eat impurities). The third type is the field crow, which is not predatory and does not eat carrion or filth; it feeds on grains and insects in fields. This type is halal. The proof includes an athar from Ibrahim that considers carrion-eating birds makruh, and a hadith forbidding the jallalah. The Hanafi ruling is that this particular crow is permissible because it lacks the harmful characteristics.

Key Terms
غراب الزرع (ghurāb al-zar‘): The field crow; a type of crow that eats grains and insects and does not eat carrion or filth.
جلالة (jallālah): An animal that eats filth (impurities) primarily.
مخلب (mikhleb): A claw used for tearing prey; specifically refers to the claw of a bird of prey.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary reason the field crow (ghurab al-zar‘) is halal?
A) It is larger than other crows.
B) It does not eat carrion or filth.
C) It lives in England.
D) It has a black color.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling on crows is based on their diet and behavior: the field crow is halal because it avoids carrion and filth, unlike predatory and scavenger crows.

Ruling on Eating the Field Crow (Ghurab al-Zar')
States ruling on field crow and provides proof from hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on the permissibility of eating the field crow and distinguish it from other types of crows using the hadith prohibition of birds with claws and carrion-eating animals.

Core Idea
The field crow is halal; the predatory and carrion-eating crows are haram.

In this passage, the author addresses a common question about crows. While most people consider all crows as unclean or haram, the Hanafi school distinguishes between different types. The field crow, which eats grain and insects, is permitted. The proof comes from the hadith prohibiting birds of prey and animals that eat filth.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and the three types of crows
Read the passage to find the overarching ruling ('no harm in eating the field crow') and the three categories: predatory crow (haram), carrion-eating crow (haram), and field crow (halal).
The field crow is specifically identified as the one that does not eat carrion or filth.
2
Examine the hadith prohibition of birds with claws
Locate the hadith of Ibn Abbas which forbids 'every bird with claws' (kull dhi mikhleb min al-tayr). This is the primary proof for the prohibition of the predatory crow.
The term 'mikhleb' refers to talons used for tearing prey.
3
Understand why the field crow is excluded
The field crow does not have such claws; it does not tear prey. Therefore it is not included in the general prohibition.
Exclusion is based on the absence of the effective cause (illah: using claws to tear).
4
Note the additional prohibition of eating jallalah (carrion-eaters)
The passage also cites the hadith forbidding the meat and milk of animals that habitually eat filth. This applies to the carrion-eating crow.
The carrion-eating crow is also prohibited on a separate ground: it is a jallalah.
5
Apply the rule: halal vs haram for each type
Based on the evidence, the predatory crow and carrion-eating crow are haram; the field crow is halal.
The Hanafi school relies on these textual proofs and the absence of contrary evidence.

There is no harm in eating the field crow. This animal tears prey, so if a human were to eat it, the habit of tearing might develop in him; therefore eating it is declared forbidden. Hadith: Ibn Abbas said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) forbade every beast with fangs and every bird with claws. Meaning: fangs (nab) are canine teeth; predatory beasts (siba'); claws (mikhleb) are talons. So it is not permissible to eat such animals and birds. Three types of crows: (1) one with a sharp curved beak, slightly white, very clever, steals chicks, tears them open—this is haram due to the hadith. (2) The completely black crow, not clever, cannot hunt, eats carrion and filth—this is also haram as per the hadith and the athar from Ibrahim. (3) The field crow, found in England, completely black, similar to sparrows, eats grain and insects from fields, does not eat carrion or filth—this is halal.
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning the permissibility of eating the field crow (ghurab al-zar'). The author begins by stating the matn: 'There is no harm in eating the field crow.' This is the general ruling. However, the author then explains that crows are of three types: the predatory crow with a curved beak (which is haram because it is a bird of prey, falling under the hadith forbidding every bird with claws), the black carrion-eating crow (also haram because it eats dead meat and filth, as per the hadith forbidding eating jallalah), and the field crow (which eats only grain and insects, thus halal). The proof for the first two types is the hadith of Ibn Abbas prohibiting beasts with fangs and birds with claws. The third type is excluded because it does not have claws for tearing nor does it eat carrion. The author also brings additional evidence from the athar of Ibrahim that every bird eating carrion is makruh, and from the hadith about jallalah (animals that eat filth) to further support the prohibition of the second type. Thus, the ruling in the Hanafi school: the field crow is halal; the other two types are haram.

Key Terms
غراب الزرع (ghurab al-zar'): The field crow, a type of crow that eats grain and insects from fields, not carrion or filth.
ذي مخلب (dhi mikhleb): A bird that uses its claws to catch and tear prey, i.e., a bird of prey.
الجلالة (al-jallalah): An animal that predominantly eats filth, such that its meat and milk are affected.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The black crow that eats carrion and filth
C) The field crow that eats grain and insects
D) The crow that steals chicks from homes

Key Takeaway
The field crow is halal in the Hanafi school because it does not have claws for tearing nor does it habitually eat carrion.

The Abqa' Crow: Why Carrion-Eating Birds Are Haram
States prohibition of the abqa' crow with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the abqa' crow, cite the primary proofs, and distinguish it from the halal field crow.

Core Idea
A bird that eats carrion is haram; the abqa' crow is prohibited, while the field crow is halal.

This lesson examines a specific ruling from the Hanafi school regarding the abqa' crow, a piebald bird that feeds on carrion. The author explicitly prohibits it, drawing on both prophetic hadith and an early athar. Understanding this ruling requires careful attention to the type of crow and its diet, as well as the legal proofs that elevate the prohibition from mere dislike (karahah) to outright unlawfulness (haram).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act under discussion is eating the abqa' crow. The ruling is clearly stated as 'not eaten' (la yu'kal), which indicates prohibition (haram) in the Hanafi school.
The abqa' crow is specifically described as one that eats carrion (al-jayf).
2
Locate the primary proofs
The author cites two proofs: (1) an athar from Ibn Tawus that birds eating carrion are disliked, and (2) the hadith of Aisha listing the crow among five fasiq animals that are killed even in the Haram.
The hadith is from Muslim (no. 1198/2867).
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah (proof implication)
The hadith's inclusion of the crow among fasiq animals and the permission to kill it in the Haram indicates its impurity and unlawfulness for consumption. The athar shows dislike for carrion-eating birds, which the Hanafis elevate to haram when combined with other evidence.
The Hanafi principle: what is killable in the Haram is impure and not to be eaten.
4
Note the ikhtilaf (scholarly disagreement)
The Shafi'i school may consider the crow halal or at least not prohibited, as they do not necessarily view the fasiq status as implying prohibition of consumption. The Hanafi response is that the crow's impurity and harmfulness render it haram.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf based on different interpretations of the same hadith.
5
Determine the mufta bihi (operative ruling)
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that the abqa' crow is haram. This is based on the Zahir al-Riwayah and the explicit statement in the matn.
The dark crow (which is less clever) is also included in this prohibition.

ولا يوكل الابقع الذي ياكل الجيف [۲۱۸ (۳۹) ويكره أكل الضبع يہ کواذی مخلب نہیں ہے (۲) اثر میں ہے۔ عن ابن طاؤس عن ابيه قال كره من الطير ما يأكل الجيف (الف)(مصنف عبد الرزاق، باب الغراب والحداة ج رابع ص ۵۱۹ نمبر ۸۷۰۲) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ مردہ یا گندگی کھاتا ہو تو وہ مکروہ ہے۔ اور یہ کو مردہ یا گندگی نہیں کھا تا بلکہ کھیتوں سے دانے چگتا ہے اس لئے یہ حلال ہے۔ یہی مصنف کی مراد ہے۔ ہندوستان میں جس کو عام طور پر کوا کہتے ہیں جو بہت ہوشیار ہوتا ہے اور شکار کر کے مرغی کے بچوں کو بھی گھروں سے اٹھا کر لے جاتا ہے اور برتن پر بیٹھے گا تو پاخانہ کر کے بھاگے گا، اور روٹی وغیرہ اٹھا کر لے بھاگتا ہے وہ کسی حال میں حلال نہیں ہو سکتا وہ ذی مخلب پرندہ ہے۔ اور اس کے بارے میں حضور نے فرمایا کہ وہ فاسق ہے وہ حرم میں بھی ہے تو مار ڈالو ۔ حدیث یہ ہے۔ عن عائشة أن رسول الله الا الله قال خمس من الدواب كلهن فاسق يقتلن في الحرم الغراب والحداة والكلب والعقور والعقرب والفارة (ب) (مسلم شریف، باب ما يندب للحرم قبله من الدواب في الاهل والحرم ص ۱۳۸۱ نمبر ۱۱۹۸/ ۲۸۶۷) اس حدیث میں کوے کو فاسق کہا اور حرم میں بھی قتل کرنا جائز قرار دیا اس لئے وہ حرام ہے۔ [۲۶۱۷] (۳۸) اور نہیں کھایا جائے گا ابقع کو اجو مردار کھاتا ہے۔ اقع کو وہی کوا ہے جو پہلے نمبر میں بیان کیا۔ یہ کالا ہوتا ہے لیکن سفیدی مائل ہوتا ہے اور گلے کے پاس تھوڑی سفیدی واضح ہوتی ہے۔ اور مردار کھاتا ہے بلکہ مرغی کے بچے کو اٹھا کر لے بھاگتا ہے۔ دلائل او پر مسئلہ نمبر ۳۷ میں گزر گئے۔ اس میں ڈر کو ابھی شامل ہے۔ اس کو ڈر کو اس لئے کہتے ہیں کہ ہوشیار کوے کی بنسبت تھوڑا ڈرتا ابقع - چتکبرا۔ الجیف : مردار، بدبودار۔
And the abqa' crow that eats carrion is not eaten. [218 (39) And eating the hyena is makruh.] This crow does not have claws? There is an athar: Ibn Tawus from his father said: He disliked from birds those that eat carrion. From this athar it is understood that if something eats dead meat or filth, it is makruh. And this crow does not eat dead meat or filth; rather it pecks grains from fields, so it is halal. This is the author's intent. In India, the common crow is very clever, hunts, steals chicken chicks from homes, sits on pots and defecates, snatches bread, etc. It can never be halal; it is a bird with claws. The Prophet said it is fasiq and should be killed even in the haram. Hadith from Aisha: Five animals are fasiq and killed in the haram: the crow, the kite, the dog, the scorpion, and the mouse. In this hadith, the crow is called fasiq, and it is permissible to kill it even in the haram, so it is haram. [2617] (38) And the abqa' that eats carrion is not eaten. The abqa' is the crow mentioned earlier; it is black with a bit of white, especially near the throat, and it eats carrion and also steals chicks. The proofs have already passed in issue no. 37. The 'dark crow' is included here; it is called dark because it is less clever. Abqa': piebald; al-jayf: carrion, putrid.
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage is a ruling concerning the abqa' crow (a piebald crow that eats carrion). The author explicitly states: 'The abqa' crow that eats carrion is not eaten.' The proof comes from two sources: (1) The athar of Ibrahim and Ibn Tawus that birds eating carrion are disliked (makruh). (2) The hadith of Aisha listing the crow among five fasiq animals that are killed even in the Haram. This indicates the crow's impurity and prohibition. The author clarifies that the field crow (mentioned in the previous lesson) does not eat carrion, so it remains halal. The abqa' crow, however, is distinct: it has a black body with white patches, and it eats carrion and steals chicks. Thus, it is haram. The author also mentions the 'dark crow' (which is less clever) as included in this prohibition. The ruling is consistent with the general principle that animals and birds that eat carrion or filth are prohibited.

Key Terms
أبقع (abqa'): A piebald crow, black with white patches, specifically the type that eats carrion and steals chicks.
الجيف (al-jayf): Carrion, dead animal flesh that is putrefied.
فاسق (fasiq): An animal that is harmful and impure, permitted to kill even in the state of ihram.

Ruling on Eating Hyena: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
States ruling on hyena as makruh and presents Shafi'i dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on eating hyena, cite the Hanafi proof, and compare it with the Shafi'i position, identifying the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
Hanafi prohibits hyena (makruh tahrimi); Shafi'i permits it as game.

Hyena (dabu') is a carnivore with fangs. The Hanafi school rules it as makruh tahrimi based on a hadith where the Prophet expressed surprise at eating it. However, the Shafi'i school holds it halal, citing another hadith that calls it game. This lesson examines both proofs and the practical difference.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Start by identifying the ruling as makruh tahrimi and the reasoning based on the hadith of Khuzayma.
The ruling is not absolute haram due to conflicting hadiths.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds hyena is halal. His proof is the hadith of Jabir where the Prophet said 'It is game.'
Game (sayd) is generally halal.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Shafi'i rely on the explicit statement 'It is game' which indicates permissibility.
They may also argue that the hyena can be hunted like other game.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response argues that the Prophet's surprise (ta'ajjub) indicates disapproval strong enough to be prohibitive. Also, the hadith 'It is game' may be specific to certain animals or abrogated.
The Hanafis classify hyenas under the general prohibition of carnivores with fangs.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: a Hanafi Muslim avoids hyena meat; a Shafi'i Muslim may consume it.
Mutual respect is essential as both rely on authentic proofs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويكره أكل الضبع . بجو اور گوہ حشرات الارض میں سے ہیں اور گوشت خور جانور ہیں۔ ان کو کچلی دانت بھی ہوتا ہے اس لئے حنفیہ کے نزدیک انکا کھانا تحریمی ہے۔ چونکہ احادیث میں دونوں قسم کی باتیں ہیں اس لئے بالکل حرام نہیں فرمایا بلکہ مکروہ فرمایا۔ بجو کے مکروہ ہونے کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن اخيه خزيمة بن جزء قال سالت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم عن أكل الضبع ؟ قال ويأكل الضبع احد؟ (ج) (ترندی شریف، باب ما جاء فی اکل الصبح ج ثانی ص انمبر ۷۹۲ ار ابن ماجہ شریف، باب الضبع ص ۴۷۰ نمبر ۳۲۳۷) آپ نے تعجب سے پوچھا کہ کیا کوئی بجو کھا سکتا ہے! اس لئے وہ حرام ہوگا۔ نان امام شافعی کے نزدیک بجو حلال ہے۔ ان کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن جابر بن عبد الله قال سالت رسول الله الا الله عن الضبع فقال هو صيد ويجعل فيه
And eating the hyena is makruh. Hyena and monitor lizard are among the vermin of the earth and are carnivores. They also have molars, so according to the Hanafis, eating them is tahrimi (prohibitively disliked). Since there are both types of hadith, it is not declared absolutely haram but rather makruh. The evidence for hyena being makruh is the hadith: Khuzayma ibn Juz' said: I asked the Messenger of Allah about eating hyena, and he said, 'Does anyone eat hyena?' (in surprise). So it will be haram. According to Imam Shafi'i, hyena is halal. Their evidence is the hadith: Jabir ibn Abdullah said: I asked the Messenger of Allah about hyena, and he said, 'It is game (sawd) and in it...
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the ruling on eating hyena (dabu'). The Hanafi position is that eating hyena is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked). The author explains that hyenas and monitor lizards are carnivorous vermin with molars, falling under the general prohibition of beasts with fangs. However, because there are contradictory hadiths, the ruling is not absolute haram but makruh. The Hanafi proof is the hadith of Khuzayma, where the Prophet expressed surprise at anyone eating hyena, indicating its repulsiveness. The Shafi'i school considers hyena halal, citing the hadith of Jabir where the Prophet called it game (sayd), implying it is permissible. The Hanafi response (not fully provided here) would likely argue that the Prophet's surprise indicates prohibition, and the category of sayd may not apply to hyenas because they are not typical game animals. The commentary follows the author's order: state the Hanafi ruling, then the opposing view with their proof, and then the Hanafi response (implied).

Key Terms
الضبع (al-dabu'): Hyena, a carnivorous animal with fangs, considered vermin of the earth.
مكروه تحريمي (makruh tahrimi): A prohibited action that is not established by a qat'i proof; still sinful to do but slightly less severe than haram.
حشرات الأرض (hasharat al-ard): Vermin of the earth, including creeping creatures and carnivores like hyenas and monitor lizards.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on eating hyena?
A) Halal
B) Makruh tahrimi
C) Haram
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rules hyena as makruh tahrimi, while the Shafi'i school permits it, demonstrating valid ikhtilaf based on different hadith interpretations.

beginner
6 min
Prohibition of Domestic Donkey and Mule Meat
States prohibition with prophetic hadith evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on domestic donkey and mule meat and cite the prophetic hadith evidence for its prohibition.

Core Idea
Domestic donkey and mule meat is haram by explicit prophetic prohibition.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on two commonly asked animals: domestic donkeys and mules. The school holds a clear prohibition based on sound hadith. We will explore the evidence and understand the distinction between domestic and wild donkeys.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? The meat of domestic donkeys (الحمر الأهلية) and mules (البغال). The ruling is that it is not permissible (لا يجوز), meaning haram.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites two hadith: one from Ibn Umar (Bukhari and Muslim) specifically prohibiting domestic donkey meat at Khaybar, and another from Khalid ibn al-Walid (Nasa'i and Ibn Majah) that includes mules and other animals.
The hadith texts are embedded in the passage.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'nahā' (prohibition) indicates that the act is haram according to the Hanafi principle that a prohibition (nahy) implies impermissibility (tahrim).
4
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
Some earlier schools held that domestic donkey was halal before the Khaybar prohibition, but after the hadith, there is consensus on its prohibition. The Hanafi school follows the explicit hadith.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The hadith are authentic and clear. The commentator relies on these as primary evidence.

گوشت۔
Ruling (40): It is not permissible to eat domestic donkeys and mules. Ruling (41): It is disliked to eat hedgehog and land reptiles. From this hadith: hedgehog (wild mouse) is not permissible, and it is a land reptile, therefore eating land reptiles is also not halal. The goat (dabb) is also a land reptile; in the above hadith it is called makruh or haram, so by qiyas the rest of land reptiles are haram. Definitions: Dabb: Goat. Land reptiles: crawling animals like mice, turtles, snakes, scorpions etc. Then commentary for (40): It is not permissible to eat domestic donkeys and mules. The wild donkey is halal, but the domestic donkey is haram. The hybrid of a donkey and horse (mule) is also haram. Hadith from Ibn Umar: The Prophet forbade domestic donkey meat at Khaybar. This shows that domestic donkey meat is not halal; it was permissible before but forbidden at Khaybar. Mule meat is haram, with evidence from Khalid ibn al-Walid hadith forbidding horse, mule, donkey, and every fanged beast. Footnote: (previous page continued) He was asked about eating it, and he recited the verse 'Qul la ajid'... Abu Hurairah said the Prophet commented on mice saying it is one of the filthy things. (a) He forbade domestic donkey meat at Khaybar. (b) He forbade horse, mule, donkey and fanged beasts. (c) He said it is not halal: horse, donkey, and mule meat.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage from Al-Sharh al-Thumayri covers Kitab al-Sayd. The author begins with the matn ruling that it is not permissible to eat domestic donkeys and mules. The commentator explains that wild donkeys are halal but domestic are haram, and mules (offspring of donkey and horse) are also haram. He then cites hadith: Ibn Umar reported the Prophet forbade domestic donkey meat at Khaybar; another hadith from Khalid ibn al-Walid explicitly forbids horse, mule, and donkey meat as well as every beast with fangs. The commentator then discusses the ruling on hedgehog (qunfudh) which is makruh according to a narration, and extends this via qiyas to all land reptiles (hasharat al-ard), making them haram. The reasoning is that the hedgehog is a land reptile, and the hadith indicates it is not halal, so by analogy all such creatures are prohibited. The author also defines terms: al-dabb (goat) and hasharaat al-ard (creeping animals like mice, turtles, snakes, scorpions). This section shows how Hanafi fiqh uses textual evidence and qiyas to derive rulings on unusual animals. The footnote on page 38 further strengthens the prohibition with additional hadith.

Key Terms
الحمر الأهلية (al-humar al-ahliyyah): Domestic donkeys, as opposed to wild ones (حمر الوحش) which are halal.
البغال (al-baghal): Mules, the offspring of a male donkey and a female horse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the legal status of domestic donkey meat?
A) Halal, because it is not mentioned in the Quran.
B) Haram, because the Prophet prohibited it at Khaybar.
C) Makruh, because the evidence is weak.
D) Halal, because wild donkeys are halal.

Key Takeaway
Domestic donkey and mule meat is haram based on clear prophetic hadith.
